O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh, most noble sons, I have completed this book which is the aftermath of the science of medicine, and have filled it with its contents, and have made the end by its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is held together by all things, it has perished along with the science and decayed, and nothing remains but the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the vanity, and the minds are closed and the knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive this treatment together with the order of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the irons of cautery, and other tools of the work with the addition of declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of all, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and the number of joints, and the movement and veins moving and resting, and the origin of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, as Hippocrates says that not everyone with the disease is very sick, and with work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that those who are not familiar with the things mentioned before, if they try to perform it, may make mistakes and harm people; so I have often seen many of those who engage in this science and abandon their science and lack of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who lanced an abscess of scrofula or a boil on the neck of a woman, and lanced the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issued out that the woman died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And another case that treats a stone from a man of age, and the stone was large; it took with him a piece of the bladder, and died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I had already been called for the extraction, and saw the position of the misalignment and the size of the stone, and if it was cut well, it would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case that took in care the Duke of our land who had the leg broken, and with the fracture got a wound; and the case plainly due to ignorance kept the fracture above the wound as a splint for a long time, and did not let the wound drain, and thus it ended; and he commanded that it not be removed early; and so it remained that the leg was completely infected and the foot and came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and dislocate his leg; and when I saw it dislocated, it was in place and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of the corruption were already confirmed or the member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another method that would crush the abscess and become infected, and then inflame due to the evil of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a pustule, when it is free of melancholic humor, does not require that one touch it with iron if it is not in a limb where one can remove everything that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	Therefore, dear son, it is important for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: firstly, where he has danger in many positions; and I will show in each chapter of this book where he has fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is important for you to keep these things in mind, so that the foolish may not speak evil of you if you take up your arms in a firm and steadfast manner, and use the best means so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are saved; and leave behind the spreading diseases of grievous sickness; and remove the doubts from your mind, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen advises in some of his admonitions: 'Do not take on the care of seriously ill patients unless you are called a foolish miracle worker.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatment into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet; and the forms of instruments, and the irons for cauterizing, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; it is ordered from the head to the feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we remember from the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of each assistant and their harmful or helpful nature.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of assistants and their harmful or helpful nature are the longest and most subtle speech and secret knowledge; and for this reason, many wise men spoke about it and agreed on this, but I do not speak much about it because I make it long.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cauterization helps universally in all conditions where there is matter, because the conditions are: it is to know hot and humid conditions with matter, and dry conditions without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry conditions with matter, they devised nothing and said that cauterization is great help; the others said the opposite: that cauterization is not helpful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat or dryness; and those who said the opposite claimed that cauterization helps greatly with hot and dry diseases that come from people's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the composition of fire, you stir the body flat.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it once by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, it does not interfere except for those who have experienced it, and who know by long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the remedies and the space of time; from other constitutions we do not have fear, specifically in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the hairs gathered together and aligned with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cauterization is a secret of healing and greater good than cauterizing medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and it only comes to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members unless named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fiery medicines come from member to another by separating, and bring diseases of great harm into the member; and perhaps the fire finds the evil, for its high heat and for the goodness of its substance does not make it, unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it has been above the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse the length of speech, because I do not like to give you the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be done at what time the cautery is to be applied, and then they should be prayed for.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cautery is beneficial in all times, because the harm that comes from it is removed by the help of the cautery; and indeed if the cautery is for necessary pain, which cannot wait until the time when greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like the foolish ones; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and they say it thus, but it is not so because cauterizations are only medicine that moves the complexion, and dries the humors that cause pain, and is worth more than any other medicine for its swift action, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the possible thing is that the disease comes again according to its nature and the part of the body affected by it and its virtue; and the superfluities are gathered in it from the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauterization for pain and similar things, and the pain does not return much; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and it is so; but they do not believe that cauteries are valid after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cauteries that are the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of those who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that the cautery of gold is more noble than iron, and they did not say why except for the quality of gold and the highness of its substance; and they said that the smell of the cautery does not cause harm, but it is not so because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some people; and a gold cauteries is more noble than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	When heating a gold instrument, do not touch it when it is hot by the color of the gold, and let it cool a little; and if it cools too much, then put it in the fire; and so it has enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	For this reason we use the fire cautery that we have already prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter about the shoulder joint from the foot, because it is lighter to find.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cauter
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is good for moisture and cold on the head, and it is done for two reasons: because of a disease called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the joint to the eyes, and to the ears, and due to many dreams and tooth pain, and throat pain, and even for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the hairs are removed by solvent medicine, changing the skin III or IV times, according to the virtues and the age and the custom of the patient, which he can suffer; and then repeat the burning of the hair.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then let him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on your palms; after that, put the root of your palm over the root of his nails between his two fingers; and where your fingers come together, if it bleeds, heat the cauterization which is called «olivare», of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the ink sign on the limb, and by gently pulling and gradually tightening your hand, then release your hand slowly, and reward the limb if you see the bone slightly; and if you do not see it, if you start again with the cauterizing tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; after taking a little silk, and putting in awe and soft cotton inside, and place on the limb, and leave for three hours; after putting on a moilliet in burre; and leave until the burn is healed; then treat the wound of the ointment which is called «tetrafarmaçon», as it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old ones said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, it helps to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should cool the cauterization so much that a part of the bone is burned, and then one should remove what is burned from the bone, and it should be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others said that one should cool the cauterization so much above, and if one removes as much bone as a spoonful of lard that women put in their flour for the reason that the humors come out wet; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards, it should be healed and treated.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good for all purposes, unless in some people where there is a way of fear; and I believe that I should leave them; because the afflicted are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and indeed when the affected part is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is safer and milder for me, and of this use I work in consequently in this way.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the main
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the main pain comes from chronic conditions that last a long time, one should use the remedies of years and pills called "cochie", and cleansing of head and eyes and plasters; and if one has done the cauterization that we have mentioned before, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take a cloth and apply it to the affected area of the patient, which is of great nature, and that it is not too hot; then cauterize with that fire brand we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After performing the cauterization on each of the horn's points up to the bone, as we have mentioned before, and perform the cauterization with the tool called «vasselz»; and place it in the part where you put suctions; and raise your hand so that you do not touch the bone: the pain from this cauterization is much greater than from others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than that with which one cauterizes the midline of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	for the fire cauterization
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	when in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease has spread to the bone, and the patient is purged by diuretic medicines, and the other treatments that I have mentioned in the division of diseases do not help: then I apply cauterization in two ways, namely with medicine or with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	the cauterization with medicine is such that you press a piece of alum, and remove the skin and put it back on the wound in two or three ways so that you can replace the piece of alum outside the skin; and when it is replaced, hold it tightly and steadily for twelve hours; then remove it and treat further with a bandage, leaving the wound for two or three days; then put on a cotton pad soaked in honey until it becomes hard.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until they are healed; and if you see that such fire-burning remedies that I have written or prescribed treat fire-burning remedies.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron cauterizer of which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the form of a clo or it has a small hook, and in the middle a small appearance; and put it on the painful limb, and hold your hand and gently turn the iron slightly, until half of the flesh is burned; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is before, and flows abundantly with blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing gauze over the wound with a bandage, and applying it to the limb for three days; then place moistened cotton on the wound, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this wound with the cauterizing iron called "cultellare", apply it at the point, and be careful not to cover the artery in this wound which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the wound
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the wound as we have previously mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterizing iron before mentioned does not cause much pain or heat, then it is necessary to extinguish the cauterizing iron called "cultellare" until it is white; and apply it to the limb in a line half an inch long, and take your hand once, and do not cover the artery and do not let it come near the bone; and be careful of the mandible that moves when turned, and the nerves should only see the moved part and that spasms do not cause pain, and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or when it is cut, there is great fear and immediately to the one who does not know, and who is not experienced; and leave the work in a short time; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this fire cauterization does not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it with the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said or from the chapter of extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this fire cauterization is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear has pain from cold, and medicines have been applied and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery called "pointed", of which is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the ear, where the pain is felt on both sides, and moving slightly away from the base of the ear, as you have indicated the punctured spot; and make X punctures around each ear; after that, cure the ear until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is only those that move from the gums, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not use cauterization for similar things that come from scars and spit of mucus.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this appearance of torture that moves from a stream of tears and spitting and choking, and it does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the pain with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a little later the temple, and the third in the jaw joint; and put the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make the cauterization above a little bit away from the horn of the ear, and another in the temple as long as a pin; and leave the cautery so high that half of the face is burned; and this is the form of the cauterization:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the resemblance of this cauterizing tool that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a bit larger; after healing the wound as I have said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the pain does not have fever, then make four cauterizations: two on each horn of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the part called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery behind the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	of laziness
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, one should give the patient large and modified brain-shaped pills; after removing the entire head of the disease, and placing the mustard plaster on the occipital region, as written or prescribed for plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is thus healthy, well; and if not, make three cauterizations of the emi to the head by descending just below the collar, and let there be space between each cauterization one inch; and the cure as with the others, and if you have seen it swollen, and the diseases are suffering, then make one cauterization in the middle; and if it is a trade, two more above the two horns, and the cure until it is healthy; and let the cauterizations which are called "olivare", as I have already said.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the chief
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the chief be cleaned of years and of the juice that we have previously said; after washing the chief of the painful part, then perform cautery on the chief and under each horn, and behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you have more trouble, and the skin is moist and the painful parts are suffering, and the disease is outside, then perform four cauteries above the spine of the back; and leave it until the most painful part is healed, and remove your hand; afterwards, cure it as long as it is healthy, and let the cauteries that are called "olivare" be what we have previously said.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization except for those that are fleaming, and it is first necessary to modify the brain from years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the pain is great and suffering from penetration of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot suffer, make them gargle and chew, modifying the brain often with good meat; then give the child water in the middle of the head, and do the cauterization as we have said before, and the cauterization on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the pain is far and suffering, do cauterizations as I have said to those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the pain is sharp, then apply the delicate cauterization as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is great, then use the cauterization of parts as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy, the excess or corrupted moisture is declining towards melancholy, and the pain is caused by wetness, then give something to drink that the mind may be cleansed, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After relieving the sharp pain; after making a good tortoise shell-shaped bandage, as a circle, and placing it on the head; if the pain increases, and is held well from all parts; then present the liniment, and use old mustard butter; and heat it gently in a fire, so that the patient can bear it; afterwards empty the circle by pushing it inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the pain every week once with another good management until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Where you have seen the fire cauterization done by making many pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the skull, and then puts on cotton moiliet in butter and in the fat of a goose.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eye's
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient the remedy that I have mentioned, keeping the head dry and washing it or bathing it several times a day while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, command the patient to turn his head, and cauterize behind the head, and do two cauterizations on the two temples simultaneously, or one if it is in one; and cover all the cauterization with all the veins and arteries that are outside the skull, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the issuing of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, then stop it with a piece of cloth.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in cutting the cauterization as you would do it; and never cautery or heat applied outside the two lower bones.
dou cors des larmes	The path of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are ancient and accustomed and are above the veins, or below the arteries that are in the appearance of the main deformed; and one sees that it is superfluous cold flabby, then apply the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter: one cautery at the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries outside the two bones; and if there is more, then wisely cauterize the sore above the bone with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	through the tears by through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not improve, then give him a draught of three poisonous herbs; after that, boil the head, and apply either the middle or the olive oil cauterization; and make two cauterizations with the «clavilis» cautery above the two sorciers, a little outside the cheeks; and guard against covering the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization called «clavilis»:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cauterization called «olivare».
de coi ci est li forme:	For this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that the second cauteries are made on the two arrowheads as long as they are; and do not leave your hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that does not touch the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Never have it happen that the hairs of the oil are converted to the pardens, and they prick at the oil, and then one makes cauteries in two ways: that is to say, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cauteries, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the hair on the safe side; afterwards, draw a line above the eyes with a figure that is as straight as the line of the mustache, and is like the beginning of the sign among the hairs; then put moistened cotton and musk oil on the edge of the skin, then heat the cauterizing iron:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing a little and a little more times, until the skin is healed in that place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreating, and the hairs standing upright; then lift your hand, and leave it so for three hours, then put moistened cotton on the burn until the blister is opened; after treating the wound until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs come after that, and the paper is softened, then begin the cauterization on that same spot again, as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural position, and is even, and do not prick at the hairs while it is growing.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauterization with burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a piece of parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and live wax, one of each, and grind them together well; and apply it hastily, so that it does not cool, then spread it over the shape you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it on the eyes; and if the patient only holds in the eye, then open it as well; and put some soft cotton moistened with water behind the eye; and the one who is sick should be in a healthy position and show his own sign above the medicine, and press the poc and the muff every time the patient feels the burning sensation of the medicine, for it feels like burning.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take the medicine at your own discretion.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blistering is passed, lift the limb upwards, and reward if you see the paper raised as it was raised by constraint of fire or by incision; and if so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply the medicine again on the limb or if the medicine has not worked, until your work is equal and your eyes are fixed; then put cotton moistened in burre over it as long as the wounds are chosen, after care, the limb of the boil which is called «dyafenis» and others, until they are healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you are in need of knowing, be well-versed in your work by great care that it does not cut into the medicine with those.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes thin after, and the hairs prick in the oil, then begin the medicine again on the shoulder that is softened with proper paper, as you have done before; afterwards cure it until it is healed; and this is the form of the fuel of the mire:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And since the eyes of men are different in size and smallness, and according to what is your constraints; and do not reply with the wrong way to that which is the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary for you to cauterize them in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Order the patient to put their head on your shoulder; and clean the wounds around their head between your hands in this way: so that they do not move, nor remove their head; afterwards, put moistened cotton cloth behind their ear or in the juice of persillon over the oil; afterwards heat the cauterizer which is ready: and place it on the head as if it were the form of a pen of feathers, together with the other which is appointed to be the cauterizer; if you see, so that it is appointed from one head to the other, and if you see, so that it is also like a tent; but whatever, this which is placed is good for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it has opened, and in its trail is the pus, and the drying; and if it is closed, if it opens, and trace further from the boil; after placing the cautery hot well, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the neck near the oil, that your hands do not go mad; and place the cautery in the grease of the oil, and corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, if you restart the cautery again, and if you have experience, and leave it three days; after that, put on gauze moistened in butter, and the cure of the desiccating ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then put on medicine corrosive tonic until the bone is discovered; and the king according to what he would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	To the fistula, and the limb; after putting in the opening a thin piece of iron with this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make of the quantity of a needle's point; and hold your hand or the iron firmly, and do not move the hairs until the points are melted and do not touch the oil; and it is good to put above the oil on the hair a cotton swab soaked in water: the iron melts the hair of the fistula, and the healthy part by wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the sinus is healed by the cauterization that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you must administer a puncture to the nose, and return the sinus to the nasal cavity according to what is proper for that limb.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are fissures in the lips that are called "hair", and simultaneously in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures as we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing iron according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the patient in those cracks until he reaches the point of release; after care, the broken bone is set as soon as it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess appears at the root of the throat or in the eye, or palate, or at the roots of teeth, after it has rotted and fermented and aged and become a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, but it does not improve: then it is necessary to cauterize according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, plug or puncture the fistula, and keep your hand on the spot where the iron comes from the source of the limb; and do so once or twice, after caring for it as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to expose the limb and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	movements of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but it does not work, then put the hot iron in your healthy hand; after heating the cauterizer in a certain way that you put a cloth on the tooth; and place the cauterizer deeply into the tooth, holding your hand steady so the pain feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then release your hand and restart the cauterizer according to your will; afterwards fill the pain's mouth with salty water, and let it rest for an hour and then repeat.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the tooth that was moving is stabilized, and the gum softened, held back, and the moisture corrupted dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain from the teeth comes from coldness, or there is coldness or wind, and medical remedies do not help, then it is necessary to use cauterization in two ways: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is such that you take butter from a fresh cow, and the end in an iron or copper spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and moisten it in hot butter, and put it on the painful tooth firmly and hold it until it is cooled; and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that moistened wool and cotton in hot butter is not enough, and put it on the aching tooth, and put it on the heated iron as far as the heat of the iron reaches the movement of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauteries are such that you can hold a hot iron or brass, and it should be large enough that the heat does not reach the mouth of the wound; after heating the cautery, because of which the form will come out afterwards, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled; do this often, because the pain will be as great that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the wound fills its mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then the raw meat; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery on the head that you wish, and according to what you have at hand; and this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	of the scaphoid:
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scaphoid bones are wet and cold, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire cauterizer of this form, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the other side; and put the cauterizer hot on the abscess once, or as often as it vies with the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cauterizer according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and put wool moistened in butter on the burn until the wound is healed; afterwards care for the wound with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the skull:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overflows through the channels of the bone, and especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then you must first evacuate the hairs by medicines that dissolve; after that, apply cauterization to the root of the neck, and be careful not to bring it too close to the neck, and do not burn too much but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply another cauterization to the joint of the neck to the base of the spine, and let the cauterizing iron which is called "clavile" be used because of its shape; and treat the limb as we have described before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the tooth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and disease of the tooth are from cold moisture, and the pain has no fever or sweat, and this is an ancient disease, then make two cautery marks on the forceps in its sight; and the other cauterization comes between the breasts; and let the cauteries which are called «clavile» according to the form that is written before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cauterization by holding the whole cauterization which is called «poins» because of the form that is written before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be just to 30, or around.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, the patient according to what has been said before, and let the burns heal in three stages according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because the burns are lighter, because you make three times as much.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, let the hairs grow over the back and over the shoulder; afterwards, relieve the pain in the area of the titillation with your right hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the burns that have two needles as follows:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound until it pierces just at the costal, and bring the four burning irons together; and because of this, the cauterization is made with the cauterizing iron that has three prongs, because the shape of the cauterization is these four prongs; and they are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and it is the form of the cauterizing iron that has three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never are they placed on this one nerve because it has eight burning irons.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After place the cauterizing iron perpendicularly, break with silk; after rest the wound, and do not move the limbs by long tension until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, this thing happens rarely, then make fire above the thick edge of the cauterizer, or many of the cauterizers in pinching.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and it is bound with moisture and is free from pain.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come into the stomach until it is at its condition, and they multiply the diarrhea in him, and are usual methods of cures and he does not improve, then it is necessary that the pain be soothed above his back, and he extends his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, apply three cauteries to the tongs, one after the other, with the quantity of a drop, at all times to the claw-like cautery, and two cauteries afterwards on the two ribs until the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and have equal space between them so that they do not join together as they go through the perforation; and let the cauteries be so sharp that they press into both parts of the bone, and let the figure of the cauteries be in this form without twisting:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see that the cauteries are being applied with a large cautery in the stomach in this form, and the one who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and holding above the stomach, and do not follow the quantity that you have seen of the needle; then cauterize with the entire cautery that is called «point».
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the cure that we have had before, as long as they are healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain from heat and moisture and great swelling, as long as it is not removed from its natural condition by excess; and the pains are relieved as we have said in divisions, and it does not help him much, then the pains should be placed above its habitual place; and a sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity over the liver, below the hypochondres, where the ears of the ox come; and there should be space between each cauterization the width of one finger; and the cauteries should be long and not press much with the hand at all the cauterization; and it should be turned only as much as the half of the body, and the pains should be placed above its feet; and if it cannot, then it should be lying down, and extend its legs, and raise its arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you wish to cauterize these cautery tools with fire, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn everything all at once, for you would make the whole body stiffer; and that it does not boil, for the flesh is very delicate there, and the skilled ones to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you know whether it is in the liver itself or in the gallbladder: if it is in the liver, it causes pain that is not too strong; and if it is in the gallbladder, it causes pain that is severe.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment is finished, it is necessary that the hairs be singed over the patient's head; then the doctor should apply a poultice where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterizing iron which is similar to a brand, because of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the cauterizing iron until the pus is removed, and it comes just to the surface, until the wound is completely healed; after the treatment according to the treatment of wounds until they are healthy; and it should only be used by this cauterizing iron by those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have never been corrupted.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it can be boldly overcome, and in all ways, it seems to me that it is worth leaving it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The fire cautery of the chest
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should use the root of aristolochia for chest cauterization in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and make sure it is dry, and also as thick and long as your finger; moisten it with oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize the wound between the armpit and the neck, and two smaller cauterizations slightly downwards on the part that is below the beard; and two cauterizations on the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a little behind; and one cauterization in front of the belly, and one between the shoulder blades, and two on the back, and two in front of the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but hold it open as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And it was said by no ancient that any man used such fire cauterization similar to the razor, and they poured water on it and put it between the ribs, until it came to the abscess; and it was so painful, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear or the pain kills now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
