si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put the instrument called "curette" into the first cut, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp edge of the instrument towards the wound and the blunt side towards the bone, and scrape until it reaches the other cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the eyes until the incision is continuous to the depth that opens the vein, and then make another incision in the same place on the other side; then extract the blood evenly, and express the lees for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton in each incision, and put moistened cloths made of wine and oil and vinegar, and guard that abscesses do not come; and the patient should lie down, and be treated with great amounts of vinegar, then the ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures that are used to treat wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	renewal of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes to have cataract surgery as usual, and you see the eyes closed and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done, there is pain, and the eyelids are swollen; therefore, by these accidents that those materials and cataract come out only from many incisions, and the movement that is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the eyelid to turn back, then make a great cut across the eyelid, and another one wide at the edge of the eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins from the temple on the right side to the temple on the left, and let the incision be just to the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, wipe out all the blood with a sponge, and then clean between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton, and linen; then bandage with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against pus forming; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to appear, then treat with things that are cauterizing, like char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of collyrium, and make a poultice; and administer it in these wounds to insert charcoal through all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that sticks in the ears is one of the four things: grains, or beasts, or stone of mine or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as peas, beans, or peas; or a running thing like vinegar and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it sticks in the ear stone or other kind of thing that does not fit well in the ear, do not let it grow in the ear, if you put the ear to the sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see an arrow, if there is any drop of purple oil or hemlock oil, then apply extraction; and the way to do this is to make them spit out their conditions, and when they sneeze, cover their nostrils, and place pieces of cloth or wool around their ear; and hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often it comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, apply extraction with thin needles, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by the thin needles, it is good; if not, apply extraction with a thin, double-edged needle; and if it does not come out by this method, make a rain gutter and blow the head of the gutter or the earwax out of the ear strongly, and stop up the ear with molten wax so that nothing can enter with the gutter; then remove it properly, for often it comes out in this way as we have said; and if it does not come out in any manner, take some glue and put it on the ears, and place some instrument that is sharp at the point to make, and put a little cotton around; then press the glue above the arrow or whatever else, and remove it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, then quickly cut the ear as soon as pus and blood come out, and spasms; and the way of the cut is that you first make a small incision in the place of the pain in the head, and extract the arrow according to its virtue, then put the pain between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the grease depends; and let the incision be as a moon, until you come to the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it vigorously to your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the following remedy in a thin, subtle form according to this method:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that small one.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make it too small when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with thin forceps and at the succession, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of earwax that falls into the ear, it is necessary to use nasal drops and clear the ear with a lot of old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the very ear itself where the sharp is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of the wind, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many thin stones according to the length of your finger and lightly heat them in the fire; and put the hairs of one's ear, or a small piece of it, on one stone, and hold it with the other hand from the other foot, and firmly press another stone against the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone by stone until the sharp is all out, and thus it will all be out; and if you see, take a thin stick, and burn one of the hairs in the ear, and the other hair grasp with fire until the thinnest stick is burned; then do the same for the others as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small in size, such as a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use pincers for extraction; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms inserted into the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the division and use distillations, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with delicate pincers, and if there are none, then take the cainne of the form that is here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And push the sharpest point in the ear according to the amount of pain, then it will often succeed completely; do this as often as all the arrows are visible.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not comply, then push cotton around the wound as I have said in the stone; and if they still do not succeed, administer distillations that the ancients have used in the opening of arrows, and you will find them where you can treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, then this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let there be silver or lead pins inserted into the small pores, and above the surfaces to drip; and to press within the distillation with a well-made lead tool for this purpose, and if you see the razor and wrap it around the tip evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see in the can, and the can should be in the ear; then squeeze through the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand evenly until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; and feel the pain inside, and let the distillations be a little warm at the fire as they are distilled into the ear; and guard that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some sort of hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by stoppage of a wound, or by a splinter inside the ear, and this stoppage never comes from within the ear, if one cannot see it; and it always comes from outside the hole, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes from within, if one cannot see it, is a bad situation in many positions, and in this one where one sees, it is necessary to put the ear in the bad position towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening completely through this space of which there is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the fire cauterize all around and behind the ear, so that it does not burn the ear; if the plug is of horn or leather of the ear, hold it with subtle forceps, and the cover lightly, until that char is completely hardened.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the plug is in the ear, take a thin, light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the leather of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the plug that the patient feels grated at the ear, slightly perforate, and make sure not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the pore, and moisten it with Egyptian mummifying oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not touch the wound until it is fully healed, or take a tent and moisten it with rose petals, and powder it with broken glass; and if you see pus coming out of the ear, then remove the tent and use another tent made of rose petals and wax, until the pus stops coming out; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood comes out, soak an sponge and wet it with cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the flow of blood which are either treating the distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper's charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the charcoal that comes from paper when it is wet and then dry, if it is necessary to extend them with tongs and pliers, and the copper of a spatula from its roots; then put it on the limb vitriol broken.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And without removing it, if the cauterize of the subtle lens cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is good; and often they are repaired, nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often in papers, one finds things that seem to be gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail," and it is an assembly of large moisture above and below; the workings are such: if the hail moves from one part to another, it is a light thing to know; then making it wide, then scraping each part lightly, then taking it as pincers, and the copper.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with copper without piercing the paper, it does not harm the patient; and if the fender is large, it assembles at a seam, and the cure as long as it is healthy; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the pain will restore it soon and cause injury.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is large and descending into the depths of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the splinter in some tweezers, and hold it with a cloth on one side and the other; and if the paper is displaced by the incision, it does not matter; and when the splinter is removed, pour some boiling salt water into the ear until the wound is clean.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is wiped onto papers above, and it has more in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears stick to their eyes; and because they lie on their faces, they sleep on their backs, and their papers are outside their eyelids moist with exinach that appears in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint to your touch and feel the extrusion among all.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs put their head in your hand; then take a cloth of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains extrusion from each part, then place it on top of them; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the extrusion is assembled within the circle; then cutting into the moisture at the spatula make a slit of a wide size, and not be any bigger than the wound made to the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the extrusion; and in many positions the extrusion comes from the slit, in the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the honey from the entire piece of cloth between your thumbs, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and be careful not to insert in the wound, that you do not bring all the poison along with the oil, that you do not harm it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not come out at the beginning of the wound, lightly scrape the wound until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then wipe the cloth with soft and rough, and put on the limb, and wrap in many layers.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who bruise the cloth and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient comes to the healer with an abscess that is not drained, then the healer should apply moistening poultices until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs are born on papers that are not natural, and are awakened, if they harm the eyes, and bring on diseases as tears and softening of the papers and the whiteness, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in four ways: either by fire together with cauterization, or by medicine according to the time before or the chapter of cauterization, and is done either by incision and stitching or by caustics, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary to place the head of the injury in your hand, then return the paper of oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a needle at the end of the thread above; and so it is on the other side of the paper or where the hairs grow between these hairs, and draw the thread above the paper, and return the scraper; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, all the surface from the great arm to the small; then extract the thread, and place outside the paper a small piece of cotton and linen, then above the paper a figure of a bandage, like the belly of a martyr, and throughout it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you saw lift the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If there is a person who has skill in cutting a great quantity of paper according to how the paper is soft; then making all the space above the two lines that you have marked, and beginning from the large calf down to the small; and let one of the wounds near the natural hairs at the base of the root, then cut the thread in one of the two angles of the needle, then scrape off the skin; then gather the two lips to a seam of an needle with all the subtle thread, and suck the blood, and dry the superfluity of the threads above the two sides at any things glueing, if you see that it is made; and if not, if you do not have care, then leave the seam and the threads just after three or four days; then cure the wound without sewing things dried and constricted, because the paper reunites to the suddenness of the wound and the assembly of it, but the seam is dry (as they say the ancients), and it is work without fear; and if another way: and that you sign the paper in a shape which is as equal to the shape of the mirror, with three threads according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then apply this remedy which is above in equal parts according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or one with a thread, and place the thread in the form; and the other thread over the great arm, and the second thread over the small one, and gather together the threads equally; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above where you have sewn, as we have told you, then gather the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar soothing substances; and once the hair of the paper has been converted: if you must use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of dogs is as follows: first, fold the paper and make two holes in it according to what I have said, then make two thin lines as long as the paper and its width; and place the two ends where you hold the threads; then bring them together subtly above the paper and oil, and strain the two needles from the two parts to form a whole; and leave it in this way for some time, and the skin that is stretched will die and rot and putrefy until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, if the coping is strong, then cure it as long as it is healed; and when the wound has been suppurated, and if the paper has been lifted, and the hairs will not grow back; and this is the form of the two needles that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a thin needle, and you boil the thread of silk softly; then assemble the hairs and pull out one and the other softly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly in the hunt, and pull out the main thread; then place the hairs on your skin so that the work is completed, for it is a subtle and delicate work, then boil the needle through the entire length of the hair at its base, and let it pierce the paper gently until you remove it from the natural hair; then stretch the hair up to the hunt, and boil the hair in the hunt, if there is one or two or three or more; then stretch your hand so that the hairs come out entirely on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not grow back with it, then treat the wound with the oil as directed, until the wound has healed completely and you can see it through the oil; then apply the oil and let it remain for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and grows on the scar; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long hair from a goat, and raise it with the other, until it is extended and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the preparation of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the "porking", comes from the oil, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by the wound, or by the barber or the cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this case is to break that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and you should only use in its cure things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	Because if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but in the work of things that soften, such as fenugreek; and the root of aquilegia or high and seed of linen are cooked, and an ointment of dayquilon melted in any of the oils, and there is wrapped a tent, and its cure is this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your care are that you take precautions so that it does not become malignant according to its former form; and this work that we have said is only intended as an introduction to this disease, that it does not return to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the ear
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental one comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you grasp a needle, in which it has double thread, and the thread in the ear, and make it pierce from the right side to the left, so that the thread comes out in the other ear; then the ear is held above all the needle, and the covering is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper returns to its proper shape according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the wound, and return the paper, and make two cuts or at the corners of the incision you have made; and let the two corners of the incision that you have made be as if they were angles so that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were a letter that has not «I greek»; then take that char, according to the quantity that its cost is away from, of what teaches the paper, then add the two missing parts and the thread of linen; then the care of what we have said about the medicines that soften, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the patient's illness comes from a cut or a stitch or a cauterization, it is necessary to make a plain cut outside of the hairs and the papers, as I have previously mentioned; then clean between the two sheets of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters apply various means of all possible methods to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and the instruments in many different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The paper is soaked with.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stitching is done by many people in a certain way, the paper above is soaked with the white of oil, and it cannot move or do its work naturally, then you should put the tip of a razor outside the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you scrape off what is hard on the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too thin, so that the pain cannot bear that the spatula is too sharp or burns the oil; and your incision, from which you scrape this assembly, should be lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and this whole assembly is healed, and nothing should ever be done in acidic salty oil, and lifted with mild sweet oil, and with collier; then put between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and put on the oil moistened wool in abundance of water; and afterwards use the collier and other things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the joint of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways the joint is affected: one is nervous and resembles a hard, dry face, and another that is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and heated with pincers, cannot be moved; both start near the large arm and grow slowly until it covers the entire eye and light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the hairs are placed in your hand, then open the eyes; and hold the paper in your hand, then bend the joint with pincers of small double strength, and extend it above; then take a needle, and put some horsehair, or cow, or beef, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the joint, and push the whole needle through the joint, and tie the joint with a thread and extend it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the joint that shows the pearl and the silk to the hair just below, then scrape the remaining at the base of the arm to all the subtle spatula and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm, so that by the incision the tears do not flow as usual; and once it was extended only to the bone, and with the thread, as we have said; then scrape all the soft tissue of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the charred flesh and break it, and that the prickle is not perceived; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk oil, and a collar made of litharge, and leave it just above the other side; then treat as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the incisions cannot enter, often this resemblance of a joint from medicines; and they are born as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, then apply oil to the pain, and take the spatula lightly with a small amount according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently rub the joint above subtly, and if you see that it does not ease and the reason is close, then drip from your mouth into the oil collier made of litargire and red collier and broken silk, and extinguish the oil just after; then begin the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk it, and cure the abscess thoroughly until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is black at night due to great harm, then pour it onto a cloth and not all at once, so that tears do not come out; then apply a red-hot iron that is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the hair that grows above the eyebrow
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men never grow red hair, and it covers the eyebrow and is held above the papers and turned to the defense, and it looks like a balcony of balauste; and the work is such that the hairs put their head in your healthy skin, then the work cuts all those hairs with convenient curves to this eye, and supports it with force; then cover the first hair, and go all scraping to the razor just at the end, and make sure you do not burn the oil at the work; and let the incision of the spatumile that we have said in the incision of the nail and as small forces of which we take the base, as it forms after this chapter the demonstration; and when the incision is made and all the hair is removed, then use the oil of silk broken or you distill red-hot iron and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil behind cotton with abin of wool, so that it is assured of aposteme; and if nothing remains, and the pain is not covered, and you doubt aposteme, then leave the oil and cure the aposteme with calming aposteme; then return to your work until it is healthy, and thus make all hairs adjusted in the oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you alleviate the care of each weakness of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that are covered over the eye, and take away from the view their work and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The work is therefore to the first that you look at this eye, in which there are red veins, and outside, and there is no other disease besides the red veins; then the work is done in such a way: command the patient to put his head in your healthy hand, then gently rub those veins all around according to his wisdom, and let the rubbing be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two times per degree in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently apply those forces in the veins, and wipe the blood away an hour after another, until you remove those forces from the oil; and guard that you do not pierce the oil with points of spatulas, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cover those forces; and when you have done this, pour green and red colloidal silver into the oil to corrupt what is left behind.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all the blood in that hour, then apply a salve over the oil of things that calm the pain of the eyes, and let it stay for some time until the pain is relieved and you are sure of no abscess, then begin again according to this method as long as they are healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror calls this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and medicine boiling according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is engaged in what you did above the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is inside, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then the instrument that is in its form; and it is called "hard head", and it should be made of iron from the same as the head, and pointed like a needle as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Place the broken bone above the joint, then twist it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the bone with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is set and the flesh grows, and the body of the bow is set and remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not infected, and no bad accidents occur, remove it when it is healed; if not, there is no other method than to return the fistula to the root of the nose according to this form: and you should discover the bone the second time with a needle and with wet medicines, and when it is discovered take the foret according to this form, and let the patient's head be fastened at three angles, and let the fistula be attenuated gradually until it is healed as you see.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone of the arm, and move your hand away from the oil and the skin, then return to the full extent of the forearm until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain as if it is coming from the inside if they hold their hand on their neck; and when the medicine has dried, as I have shown you, and when the char is born and hardens the muscles, then apply the matter to the neck; it is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open wide and do not close, and it does not disturb the neck or cause discomfort, then you must bind the pain; then cleanse, then apply leeches or hot compresses to draw out the pus, then place the oil on a mixture of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply it with bandages and cloths; the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are sufficiently soft and double each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes have needed; then strain it through a cloth that is very hard and form, and start the leeches again to draw out the pus without causing harm; then remove the leeches and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the pain remains, it is good; if not, restart the application of bandages, cloths, and leeches until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the tearing of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the vein, it is opened and there are many papers like a piece of resin, and it is unsightly to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you should insert a needle into the root of the part below this above, then insert another needle or a double thread of the arm part; and perforate it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then tie the double thread around the part of the vein, and hold it well, then remove the needle and put some oil mixed with honey on the wound, and let it stay until the thread is cut with the vein, then care for comforting things until the wound is healed; and never restrain the wound by a bandage of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly swollen, pierce them with a fine needle that comes from under the oil, and wring out the moisture of the albuginea and descend upon the eyelids, and enter immediately; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from under the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease that is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a bubble that is assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp descent, and it is not sharp; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the pain sit on the seat prepared and straight, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and the movement as much as you see the bubble come to the top of your eyes; then let it go, and do not descend and do not be disassembled by the light, and see the things as they were; and if they do not descend, it is sharp, and if the things that descend from the bubble are not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you hold the hurt part between your hands, then take the fine spatula and place it under the cornea, and with the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the eyelid, until the hole is closed; and when it is closed, then pour hot oil mixed with honey, or hot honey or fenugreek, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have had similar cases in the division, and what is needed to pierce; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the hurt part sit between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and the healthy oil tightly; then put the paper of the oil to your right hand if the eyes are crossed, or to your left hand; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are crossed, the instrument called «almagda», or to your left hand, if the eyes are not crossed; then place the point of the instrument above the cornea by the thickness of a thread in the blemish of the oil at the part of the minor arm, then strike the instrument called «almagda» vigorously, and keep your hand until it pierces the blemish of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the beginning of the space that is from the gold to the end of the needle; and this is the cornea of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument above or the hot oil.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is now sharp-sighted, he will see the hairs before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if he is now sharp-sighted again, put the flame with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not move, gently turn your hand back and forth; then put a small amount of cotton on his eye and leave it inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eye is cleaned with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil and plenty of water, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our household, put on top of the wound with plenty of water.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are men who have very hard eyes, then you must use the tool called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore, pierce only the conjunctive part, and do not let it move too much in front, but make the eye sleep subtly, then gently open the hardness, as we have said; and at the end of the work compare the patient's condition to the drowsiness that occurs, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie it according to its disposition just after midnight; then release him in the same dark house, and check his sight, and show him some things, and then return the bandage to the next day; and you should not do this in the morning of the care or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise the eyelid, for the sharp pain.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should apply hot oil before the seventh hour, and strengthen it with what quenches abscesses; and when it is calmed, remove the cloth and put a new one on its face to cover any opening, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go out of the house little by little, and convert it into its own case; and do not let any disciple intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Some came to us who was of the Yrach, who told us that in some countries people did something called a "lancet", because of which the wound heals, but I never saw any in our land, nor have I read anything about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almonds, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure tin.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they have the same thinness in their heads and the backs in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the char for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do they grow or appear as noses that are twisted in various ways, of which there are some that resemble scorpions at the top; and if there are such, or if there is a swollen nose of bad color, and if there is a soft nose of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of those noses that are soft and not twisted, it is necessary that you make the pain between your hands against the sun; and work their nostrils, and pour the quicksilver into those noses, and take them out; because this is what you can support with the subtle ague of one part, until you see that that nose is all healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains nothing that can be removed with subtle and delicate instruments, then open it completely; and if it is an abscess, clean it as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the wound is no longer wet and all the pus is removed, then pour or wash with vinegar and water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it opens in the palate, and moisture enters into the palate, then wipe it clean; and if it does not perforate as it should, then there is a bone above, to which instruments do not come out to cut: therefore you must go with a piece of linen thread a little thick, and be careful of your hands, and have space between each nail as much or as little; and put the bad parts of the thread in the mouth of the patient, and draw it through the nose until it comes out through the nostril; and many times they do this with children in schools, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the part that comes out through the nostril with one hand, and the other part that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and clean them alternately as we have done.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the newts have not corrupted that cloth, then remove the filth, dampen the blood, and moisten the thread with an Egyptian eye salve, and return it to the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of the cloth; then place or put a plaster on the nose for several hours until it is healed, and if it requires medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a cup, and the conduit is also used in this way; and if you see, make a closed cup, and let the instrument be polished to purge the head; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the head to the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease arises in the head of the nose that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large to the point where it looks like a thing; and because of this, it is necessary to cover it at the beginning, and then put the hot iron or the burning medicine on it; and if it is difficult to cover it when it is large, if it is hard, of poor color, and has poor sensation: if you do not touch it with iron because it is a hidden abscess, for when you cover it once, great harm comes to the pain; and if the abscess is softly touched, not with iron color, and you see that you can completely cover it, then remove the pain and the covered thing, and cure the nose of similar and restricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	there are many solutions that come in one of these cartilaginous parts, which is only slightly beneficial to some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, if the wound is fresh and full of blood, then look to see if the lips are split on both sides; and then stitch them together, and care for it until it heals; and if the lips are already scarred on one side or the other, then you must burn all the parts that are not healed, then assemble the two lips together, and hold them in place, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and frankincense; and put the powders on a piece of strong plaster or another plaster bandage, and let it soak through, then care for the wound until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you assemble the thread: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses inside the lips, which are hard and small, and smaller and larger; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut under each one, and take out the pus with forceps and clean every part; then apply the wound after incision with broken glass ground, until the wound is no longer wet; then apply a poultice of dry things until the wound is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the toothache
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.
