Many times, toothache arises from the gums being injured, which the ancients called "albulus"; therefore, it is necessary to support it with forceps, and cover its root, and let out the pus or blood; then put on the affected tooth vitriol crushed, or other powders that strengthen and dry; and if the toothache returns after the incision, and often does, then cover it again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never assemble teeth at the root of the tooth, between the gums, and the sharp and unpleasant scarces; and sometimes black and yellow and green teeth are between the gums, as corruption comes to the gum, and are foul-smelling teeth. So you should place the pain between your hands, and its roots should be in your holy place, and cut off the teeth or the scarces that appear, until nothing remains; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is at the first layer, it is good; but if not, start again from the second day and the tool, until you have removed everything; and be aware that teeth have various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the work shows, because the razor that removes teeth has different forms than the one that removes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When treating a tooth for pain that you delay drawing as much as you can, because no one should do this; for it is a very high substance, so we have no excuse to draw.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the tooth is forced to be drawn, you should be certain of the tooth's root.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the tooth is relieved, and one should be careful that it is a holy tooth, and draw the good tooth; and then the pain does not depart, until the evil is extracted, for we have already done this to these saints; and when you are certain of the tooth's root, it is necessary that you scorch around the tooth in all directions; then loosen it with your fingers or subtle forceps at the first and second point, until it is well dislodged, then firmly hold the forceps; and let the one who has the tooth in their mouth between their teeth, and hold it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump back, take one of these tools and push it gently into each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and broken, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the holes are; and if the extraction is subtly attached to the teeth, so that it does not break when extracting; and it is very important to cover around the gum to relieve the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and again give the pain by the greater evil of the root more severe pain from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant physicians who, by their haste and audacity, break the cart once and for all, and do not bring back what we have told; but they bring about great disease through the roots that they delay, or through the cart that they break, as we often have seen; and when the density is drawn, if blood comes out, which often happens, use the wound with boiled wine or vinegar and salt; and if it continues to come out, use the wound with vitriol broken; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long and broad, so they do not double back when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick enough so they do not bend when you pull, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have sharp teeth to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then you must place soft cotton moistened in oil or water on the wound.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is softened, then pull the pliers which are called "algefri", of which the patient seems like a beak; and they should be made inside like a wedge and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these needles, it is necessary that you scrape around the root entirely, and there you put the instrument called "althali", which is a spoon, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too large so that it does not break in half, and if the root jumps out through the hole, it is good; if not, if you help with all the instruments, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other forceps that are before in the range of the teeth, and with this instrument that seems like large needles, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument should not break, and it is sharp with many instruments of dense material; and also other instruments, which are not counted among them; and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease demonstrate, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument for the diversity of them, and if they break the cart or other bones, or if it hurts, if they search for instruments that are necessary, as I have said, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be strong and well holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and remove; then restore the limb with medicines suitable for it, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then use this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you remove the tooth after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and no one can be made or polished: then use this tool; and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this tool which has the shape of a small beak, and it is similar to the small beak, and it is made of iron and sharp at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper is slowly and slowly placed in the mouth for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that one can be removed, then the copper is removed with a small force as follows:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the copper of which the needles are made; and in this way, the copper is slowly and slowly placed in the tooth for a short time, so that it does not move until it pierces; then the plane is used at the end to remove any roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then the sharpness must be removed until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they are pulling teeth
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when they are pulling teeth, either by percussion or by falling out, and the pain cannot be restrained from the jaw that it does not chatter, and you treat them with restrictive medicines, but it does not help; then you should restrain them with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and rotten, but the gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth approaching each other, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the affected teeth between the healthy ones, as many as there are or more, until you reach the other side of the healthy tooth; then begin to cover the part where you started, and gently and skillfully restrain your hand, so that it does not move at all; and let your wire be tied to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the broken tooth with a thin wire, and assemble it, and place it between the healthy tooth, and keep it in such a way that it does not bleed the tongue; then keep it so tight as it can hold, and if it slips, or the wire breaks, then tie it with another wire; if it holds, it will serve in such a way throughout its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two missing teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth breaks, if it is reset in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and it does not interfere with any part that is not wise and suffering, and never once is the shape of a bone tooth of a goat made, and it is placed in the place of the defect, and it is kept tight as we have said, and it holds and serves in such a way throughout its length.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut through the cartilage of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no time when the cartilage of the tongue comes out of its place naturally or by nature, as it is born with it; or by accident of a wound; and the works are such that you cut through the wound of the mouth, and hold the head in your own, and lift the tongue; then cut through the nervous cartilage of the wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or not, and it is by severe wounding, if you boil the herb and cut through the wide gently; and beware that the wound does not become too wide, for the artery which is outside; and when you have done, lift the head of high rose and vinegar, or high cold water, then put out of the tongue a linen tent; and treat the wound each night, so that the wounds do not stick together.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If blood comes out, put broken glass on the wound; and if it does not stop bleeding, cauterize it with slow-heating iron, which is good for the wound; then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the wound is of a yellowish or black color and hard, and if it does not hurt, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to discharge pus, and there is moisture, pour water through the opening, and wipe it with a thin sponge, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if it does not stop bleeding at your work, put broken glass on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you remove all the blood; then lift the wound off the bone and tendon, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never come from within the throat blisters that are called "godath", and they are properly called the II mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful: if it is an abscess hard of small size and of pus color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, as for the running of blood; but let it be until it is soft, and then you will break it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first check if the abscess is at rest and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the misaligned part in front of the sun, and his head should be straight, and the work the mouth and the prick between his fingers, and press the tongue out of the way from all the instrument, from which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine iron as some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the needle and the hook in the amber, and draw it out as high as you can; and take nothing with you from the cloth, then cover the instrument, of which this is the form, which seems like a forceps; and all the head is bent, and one place another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool present, use a pair of tweezers, which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side, it is sharp, and on the other side, it is blunt; and when you have removed one of the thorns, remove the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the sharp thorns with hot, sharp, and salty water, and if there is blood that comes out, gargle the sharp thorns with hot, sharp, and salty water, or use pounded green pomegranate skins, or mint leaves, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then treat the wound as it becomes healthy; and once in a while, other abscesses do not form in the throat except for the two thorns, so remove them in the same way as the two thorns should be removed.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged deep within her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the swelling, and could not eat or drink, and died if she remained like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had already been drained twice through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore acted quickly, and inserted a probe into one nostril, then removed the pus through the other nostril, and cut out a large portion of it; then I repeated this process in the other nostril, and pressed on her tongue; afterwards I inserted the probe into these abscesses, and removed a part of it, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus the woman was able to breathe again, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at this abscess for a long time; the abscess kept growing back, and filled up the cavity that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I inserted a probe and cauterized it inside her throat: thus she was able to breathe without growing again; and I removed these parts and left only God to deal with them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When looking at the eye, and it is protruding and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not too large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	If the eye is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, and you see that the abscess is calm, and it is thin, then you should squeeze it; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or red or black, then you should avoid incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in pricking it.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its size and length, you should place the hairs in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then make an incision in the gum, and remove it, and cover it with one or two of the instruments that I have mentioned for the incision of the two nails.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you only cover the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cover more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two nails, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pains are too great for the patient to bear, then it is necessary to use a cauterizing instrument to relieve the pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on the safe side, and then presses the tongue against the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confuses it with very hot water, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in the movement of this instrument, which is shaped like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the patient should have a hair or something to hold the medicine, like the tines of a fork, and places the instrument on top of the medicine over the uvula; and the patient lies on his side, so that saliva and muscle from his mouth flows out of the medicine inside, so that it does not drip down his throat and cause bleeding; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it over the uvula for half an hour, until you see the benefits of the medicine and the wounds are healed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument through all the cotton into the throat, until the cotton is dry on the uvula; and do this repeatedly until the cauterization of the medicine is complete, then let it dry for four or five days; and if you have to restart the cauterization of the medicine, start again, and after the cauterization moisten it around the uvula with wadded cotton and burr, and clean what is around the medicine; and be arosed with very cold water, and be treated with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer from incision than cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and all or some of them in a pot, and put honey in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the pot have an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or copper, and one of the pricks pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the wound through the nose, until the wound is dead; afterwards, repeat it often until the wound dries, and keep in mind that you do not make this steam at the beginning of the onset of an abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this steam except at the decline of an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cloth and place inside the head a piece of ice, so that the patient's mouth is not too much chilled; for the piece of ice does not make too much steam to burden the mouth, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it is necessary to remove bones or spines of fish, or nothing at all; so you must take what you can see and press the tongue against the sun at all instruments, so that you can see the thing; and what does not open you and is returned in the throat, you must make vomit the bad thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is removed by vomiting; or the bad things swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the throat, it will stick, and then pull out the thing; and if it does not come out of what we have said, take the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Let the instruments be curved at the end so that they can more easily enter the throat, and raise the head high; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, that it does not come into contact with it, or push the bone inwards; and it is better that the hairs push the instrument, because it is more likely to be the thing that is causing the problem; if it goes down, or it pulls it out entirely, evenly along the entire instrument, as far as it can go.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's lining
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	The throat's lining is never treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not help, then look at the throat's hair to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the shoe, if it is made with all small nails, or with thin tongs that are worth a penny.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth a penny, take a hair rope, and beat the evil one in the throat with it, then beat or move the iron as often as you can.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the evil ones are all tired during the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full bucket of cold water, and work the mouth, and pour it down so that he does not swallow, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the shoe feels the cold, it will drown.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If it does not stick as we have said, then smear the wound with asafetida, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will stick without glue.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation is that you hold the pot or where there are visible coals, and place a cloth perforated in the middle over it, and in this puncture put the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the wound in the mouth of the can, and close the mouth, so that the fume does not escape but goes up through the nose; and the nose will now hold, and if it does not stick, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink any vinegar; and then the matter is that it should be cured by this regimen.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat the throat, which is, when one can see it, similar to curved hooks to enter the throat; and it resembles a beak, and it has a roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot slip; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are various types of abscesses, according to what memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways that the one is in its own shape itself, and because it retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those who are at the neck.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those at the base, and the abscesses of the neck are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is dead according to its completion; and if there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is surrounded by, perhaps because the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which it is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located away from the main limb, and if you delay puncturing it until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is located away from the base, if you puncture it before it dies, it may not be able to stand, and it will remain crooked inside, and there will be a fistula; and it cannot be healed in the long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary to remove the discharge from the puncture of the abscess that is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and inflammation, and the debatement and the relief of the main abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary to make the puncture wherever the abscess is most dependent on the limb, and where it opens most easily; and let the puncture be long along the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the throat, it is better to leave the incision until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it beforehand, the blood from it will flow along with the veins, and it is plagued by much filth; and perhaps harden the lips and penetrate into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is pierced according to the wide vein, as the member has need of it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is appropriate to treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses with large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or it is necessary to cover them, and close; when they have become as soft as cloth, and are dead, then it is appropriate to do so as one does with boils: and if there are such that are cut in three angles, and if there are such that are covered as the skirt of a mantle, as abscesses of arrows; and if there are such that make a round cut, and other cuts and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	If they do not have a chief, as in the case of a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you puncture it clearly; and if the abscess is large, and has a great deal of pus, and you puncture it, you must not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only part of it; then suppress the abscess on the following day, then do nothing else; do this repeatedly, as often as necessary, until all the pus is drawn out; especially if the wound is of weak strength, or if a woman is carrying it, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the patient should never be raised too high with the release of the bow, for by chance the patient may die from the pain, and you would not be blamed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, moisten the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a simple sore, treat it with linen or woolen cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you fill each one with old cotton or shreds of linen to keep moisture away, and tie it to the body; then open, and treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flows from your work, apply sharp cold and cooling ointment, and wipe the wound, and place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood flow persists, apply government and healing ointment, and use the powders I mentioned in this book, and if it is very painful, and if the wound or abscess is very sensitive, it is best to cover with tents and wipe with wine and oil; and if it is in a state of decay, and the wound is charred, it is best to cover with cloths moistened in cold water, or with wine and oil, as we have said; then drain the abscess and dress it, and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the body, and there are ways that are in cloths, such as the lancing of a boil, and very many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such ones that are moist like chicken; and if there are some that are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the belly is such that you try all instruments called "intromissions", from which the form comes after, a thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they make it through above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off any hair that contains that moisture, for it will return if you leave anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply to the wound, and leave it there overnight; and this will correct what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are sure that it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess is not large, then cut it according to this form, from long to short; and pour in your needles, and scrape the skin from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it is. And if the artery makes it opposite, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this with an abscess if it is pierced, and cut and treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting above an abscess, if it is less painful, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to any of these abscesses or swellings or there is no moisture, and among these were the abscess I copied or from an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard, rough, and white as a stone, and could not break it; and if one had tried to cut it, one would have made just as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or from the swellings, because those that come from the chin and roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, to let out the pus; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscess on the neck, and discharge pus, and inflammation, and sometimes appear elsewhere in the body, and are very painful, and are inflamed together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own side, like the neck and abscess of the head, as we have said; and similar to these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are harmful and do not wish to follow health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the flesh, and is immovable from every part and is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape off the skin from each part, and keep the two lips of the wound as even as possible, if you have the skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and slowly and carefully, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and not too deeply, that the hand does not escape, and not too soon, before you cover what you do not need to.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you puncture the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to open it, put in the wound vinegar broth, or some powders that stop bleeding, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is healed, and then begin to purify.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work until you complete it; then consult your knowledge if there are any small abscesses remaining, and puncture and drain them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the abscess, it is only necessary that you puncture that abscess at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through it without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire pustule, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and hold them in place, as there is no remaining superfluity due to the size of the pustule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cover the root of it with a covering, and draw out the core, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those pustules that contain superfluity, prick them where the core is still alive; and prick them thus, as we have said before, depending on the situation, then apply ointment and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well covered, the cure of ointment continues until it is healed.
de squinance	of dizziness
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the choker of the throat; but I never saw such a thing in our land, and it is their written account.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have dizziness, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and because all veins and the pore of the evil are in those who have abscess full in the mouth, or in the throat or in the hollows.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it out of three circles or four, with a small incision through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision through the soft part, not in the cartilage; and those who are thus cut in the section of the epiglottis have no scar, and the wound is long healed.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the neck all around, then cuts the cartilage until it comes to the chin; and avoid the veins of blood, if you see anything, and then cover the soft part, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the throat stream which jumped through the bone that was broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which one doubts strangulation, gather both lips of the wound together, and cover it completely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause blood to flow, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stiffened, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect has left the body.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, one should cover the epiglottis for this reason that the limbs cannot be kept, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they commanded the ancient ones to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And therefore they commanded to sew the wound and cure, as long as it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and stabbed herself in the neck, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not bled from the vein or the wound, blood flowed from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I quickly bandaged the wound, and healed it until it was cured; and she did not die because she was able to speak, and returned to her usual state; because I believe that in the tissue of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "hernias of the throat", and are large abscesses in a yellowish color, and are common in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; or natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is in two ways: one is similar to a large swelling, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from us through an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be opened except by a small incision, and the proof and search are throughout the entire incision: if you find it as I have said, and cannot be removed at all, then treat it as we do with abscesses, and remove it entirely, if there is any; and search well and treat it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	For the fire cautery
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many methods of us are, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I tell the whole difference between us and the other.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the other is cold and feverish, as long as the boils have not passed, and is accomplished by the purgation; therefore the fever and the cold rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is neither cold nor fever nor pain, and it contains the spleen, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a small thing, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, whether dry or wet, and much of color are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the care of a new patient, it is necessary to first examine and try the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form as found in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of examining abscesses is that you press or more moist skin than you pierce in the abscess, and return your two fingers slowly, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful that it does not slip.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running wound is colored, as I said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire does not come moisture, then it is fat, then cut it in a cross, and take pincers, and scrape lightly from each part and wipe the coat or where you should remove it clean with the new; and if you cannot remove it clean, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if nothing remains, it returns to us many times; and if it stays for a short time, and does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, close the wound, and place soothing things on the abscess, and treat other wounds until they are healed; and if it is large, cut out the two lips of the wound, and treat what causes the infection.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it beats against you or another, and you are in a hurry, apply the broken glass of vitriol to the wound, and let it remain for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the wound from the blood; then return to the copper that was left.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of instruments for extracting splinters, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to extract splinters from abscesses; and they are like the needles that one uses for sewing, and are made of brass, or iron, or silver, and cost as much as those that are yellow, and are more effective for extracting splinters from boils; and they are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the pustules.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the needles are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are needles with two prongs in three ways; and if there are needles with three prongs, and they are also in three ways; and if there are needles with two prongs, and one prong only, and they are also in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The sharpness of these is to cut, and there are some that do not cut much except from one part, from which we scrape the skin, so that we do not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these puncturing instruments are the needles with rounded ends, so that the patient does not suffer at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and no other instrument is used except in fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar places; and never made another instrument small, resembling skin scrapers for evacuating blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never put back in place which should have healing contact with the veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as they seem like breasts of a woman; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line b. to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with healing medicine using charcoal, then sew together the two lips of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast falls down, and is molded due to its great size as in women, and if the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line b. to g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not made completely, because the pains do not want to rest, or due to the drainage of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened cotton swabs in a corrosive ointment; and let it remain until it absorbs the remaining fat and the ointment, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the hocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the hocks are hard lumps or have ribs, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it there for a day, then remove all the cotton, and treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to pustules, then treat them as we have said about incising pustules, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is hard and swollen, then often there are abscesses, and just as much blood in the vein and abscess; and if you know it is for the artery, then treat the abscesses long and even; and when you feel it with your fingers, it is stiff; and when it is for the vein, it is reddish and swollen; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside the tendons and bones and muscles and many other parts, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is in charge should also avoid it, and in the one who is inflamed with arterial blood flowing through the long skin; then open the abdomen as one would with a needle, and sever the artery of the cloth until it is exposed; then insert a needle on the other side, and pierce it with another needle from the other costeit, and hold the artery with a double thread in II leus, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not touch the flesh that is between the two liens of an intromissoire until the pus that is inside comes out, and remove the abscess; then treat the cure that has been inflicted, as long as the lien chient; then treat the cure of oignement that is appropriate for this, until it is healed; and if the abscess is in the belly of the vein, if you have pus on all the skin, then dip your hand in the pus from the abscess, and pull out the needle, and there should be a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other costeit; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or with the two ends of the thread of the one that is in the other part of the two needles; and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then put another needle all the way through the pus at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four leus; then cover the abscess until the excess is inside, then cover the superfluity of the cure and leave what is tied; then put a moist cloth on wounds and treat the cures of tents and oignemens until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
