Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often happens to the helpers and the dose in all of them where there are joints, and this is very painful, and its color looks like the color of blood, and it is in many positions with pain; and when they strain it, if they feel the pain, and it is not from the body, but outside of the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, or outside or above, and those who are in joints do not need to cover them with iron: perhaps there is contraction; and those who are on the head or face, making the skin pale.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if it has a point to a needle, and cut at its root; and if it is large, if it is suspended from the top, and scraped, then the bone and assemble the wound at the seam, and cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large tumors hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never found in bellies and never in any other part of the body, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has a subtle root, and large swellings; and there are small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were growing due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one weighing eighteen ounces, and in the other six drams, and the work in the incision is that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the arrowhead is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide spatula, and it is in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood if you do not see the hairs, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the hair spouting and painful from the incision of the iron, take good thread and tie the arrow as we have said, and let it be for two hours; and then restrain, and do not stop pulling the thread through until it covers the arrow, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, then use the copper itself for the belly, but you must also cover half of it, then cauterize that it does not return; then care for the wound, and guard that you do not cover the thread which is of pale color and poor sense and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is some abscesses which become infected, and I will come to the treatment of wounds after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the foot is injured,
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the foot injury comes from the wound or cut of the foot, and it is above the belly and in some of the swellings, as it has in other wounds, of blood which cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of pus; and if it is from the tear of the foot and from the outlet of the feces, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the purpose of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides so that it returns, and then it comes back, and perhaps if it is torn, and expands greatly at the entrance of the bath and for great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain much; and if it is for an arrow, it is open by these signs of large and hard abscesses, and is filled according to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the wounds are such that you look to see if it is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave, let them care for themselves.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the abscess, then you must command the patient to dye his hair, and be extended straight out, then sign all around the belly; then place the infected part above the great umbilicus; then tie it tightly with a strong silk cord, and let the intestine hang down; if you find the intestine, take it out and hang it behind the stomach; and if you find the abscess, cut off the excess and put it in a container; and if the artery or vein makes you go against it, then quickly go around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and make the patient hold them as if you were going to pierce; then strain the abscess into four parts above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the wound until it can heal, and let the dead tissue die by itself; or take it away when it has become thin and ready to fall off, then cure the wound as we have said; and strain out the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the wound as it should be, and suture the wound.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the division about the similarities of chancre, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how to use iron cure; and we say that chancre should be treated with caution, and warned the ancient that when chancre is in a place where it can be removed as if it were a chancre that is in the breasts, and in the chest, and similar places, and one must remove everything when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, then it does not matter that you approach it, for I have never been able to heal any; and no one has ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you remove once the evil of black bile; then cleanse if it has manifest repletion, then bathe the wound in good blood to perform the operation; then pour your ointments or chancre, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe well the wound with your hand or any thing, and if the flow of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the blood is stopped; then treat other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	For hydropy, instruct the patient to let the h
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	In the division of hydropsy, we have mentioned the resemblances of hydropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the acute is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the treatment by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only swelling; and one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarcoce, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this resemblance of hydropsy which is called "swelling" by medicines, and the cure does not work, if you look at whether the pain is weak, or if he has another disease besides hydropsy, as vomiting and similar things; then do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the pain of great virtue, and he has no other disease except hydropsy alone, and he is not too old nor too young, then thus: gently lift the pain upwards with your hands, and the assistant presses the belly by bringing the acute to the lowest part of the worst, then take the spatula in the form of a spoon:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And cutting of two parts at the tip, and ensure that no part is too thin so that it can reach the intestines when thrown, and cannot be bleached; then check if there is hydrops near the intestines: if it is for the disease of the liver, then make your incision on the right side of the third rib three fingers above the shoulder; and if it is for the gallbladder, then make it on the left side of the third rib three fingers above the shoulder, and it should not be that the hairs grow on the incision so that the superfluous do not run to the weak liver; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and boil, and remove your hand from all the space between the skin and the gallbladder as if in scraping at the quantity of an angle or around; then pierce the gallbladder until the space comes to the desired length, and that is the two edges of the blade, then remove this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is of light rain or chalk, and has in its part below three small holes; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the one who sews it is cut as with a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make to cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the above is the needle, so that when the instrument comes to the point, then it should be inserted now above the instrument; voiding the half or the third part, because if you remove more than it is necessary in that hour, by chance if the patient dies from the resolution of his spirit of the arm, or he faints, or approaches death; but according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the wound signify, and its pricks; then take the instrument and retain the point, and it is retained now for the one who strikes the hole that is above the syringe, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take a small quantity of the point; do this every day, and guard against following it too much until it is only a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the pain, and leave it for a long time, the cure of the sepulture or sand chafes, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and becomes tanned; and the cure of desiccative medicines as long as they are healthy, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born who does not have some pertuss in the rod, or the pertuss is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce very thinly throughout the entire length according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or pierce very thinly through the bottom, and bind it and keep it thus for three or four days until he wishes to urinate, then remove the closure, and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it does not suit, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is pierced is small, then treat him with a thin piece of cloth from the bottom, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who have not yet pierced in their own flesh are called "blecets," because no one is born with a piercing at the top of the penis, so they cannot urinate before their penis rises; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the marriage, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie evenly on their backs, with the head of the knife and the copper plate like the width of a quill, so that when the wound cuts in the middle, it is done as it should; and beware of letting blood flow too much, and if it does, if the water that comes out is blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pus from the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times worms come in the knife, and it is an appearance of a bad smell; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; if you must take them out with a delicate hook, and clean and remove all, then put on cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if it is a malignant ulcer, black and putrid, then you must apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the ulcer is deep within the flesh and has spread to both sides, then you must first remove the part that is inside; and when it is healed, then treat the part on the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, if the ulcer is not healing, and it becomes blacker and more corrupted, and there is pus, then remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from grape scum and eggs, then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	If bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterizer should aid in two dispositions: at the onset of bleeding and during corruption; and if the prick is corrupted and drawn back, it is necessary to apply a piece of cloth soaked in piss between the wounds; and when the flesh has reached the head of the rod that has not yet been circumcised, or if it is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to scorch it with the tool until the ligaments are loosened, and the prick is delivered from all parts of the rod; and if this is a difficult matter to decide, then it is necessary to scorch it with the tool at any point above the head of the rod and the skin; then thoroughly clean between them, and apply a subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not recur.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not of the same importance as other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest in terms of health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and sages who performed circumcision in the time of the ancients, and at forces, and all at once; since it was the most careful one because it had two threads, and perhaps if one coped with the other, it would delay the one outside.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is prolonged, and the pain is doubled, and the mundication which is done with oil does not always ensure the point of the member; and the mundication of the wound by chance may escape the iron, and corrupt the work, and many times it happens that they are born in such a way that they have no need of mundication.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mundication which is done with force to all the length of the thread, I have found the best of the experiment, for the forces cut as much from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the length of the thread; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and that the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he listens, that you are only binding the thread around the rod as much as possible, and then throw it in all ways that you can; then bring the thread straight between your hands, and press the forces between your hands or outside your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then close your hand on the rod and blow gently, and take it up as high as the end of the rod is; then clean it well of the dirt which is gathered there, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it outside one end to the other end; and take the two ends to the second work at the pouch and the proper index, and cover between the two ends, then lift the gently and take the head of the rod; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on top and top the powder with a poultice made of a piece of bread cooked hastily with red wine vinegar, confit with rose oil and fresh, and leave it there until the other day, and cure the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for the healing process is as follows: both shoulders should be held tight and stretched, and they should be kept equally as strong as the other.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the healing process is when the fingers are bent during the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend them at your angle, as well as the other fingers, and if you cannot hold them at your angle, then use splints and then the coping.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they stay for three days, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscesses have healed, and scrape lightly; and if you can move the coping as you please, and guard against the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the limb of things sordid wound from powder, that we have said or treat of powders, and if one copes with care beyond measure, and it goes above, so it will not harm; cure then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retaining of the urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of the urine is by oppression of the stone, or of blood congealed, or of bowels, or of charred, or of similar things, that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention by the stone which is high or col of the bladder, then it is necessary that the pain be raised above his knees; and his feet are put on his back, and his belly is extended from the part above the back, and restrains the pain as much as he can; and therefore the bladder's neck is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is released, and if it does not come, as we have said, and the pain is great, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it is of fine silver, thinly beaten, like the quill of an owl; and it is of a palm length and half, and it is thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it at the head of a linen or cotton cloth, and push the head of the thread into the tube; and cover the excess of the cloth and push it towards the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair, and the arise the urine and the stick of moist oil and oil of olive and vinegar; then place lightly the tube in the stick, until it reaches the root of the stick, then double the stick over towards the edge; then push the tube ahead just next to the cloth, and the patient feels the urine coming next to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except when the conductor or she goes is twisted; then stop the thread at every linen pocket and pocket, and the urine follows the cloth, then extract it, and correct the urine; and begin the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood enters the bladder, or putrefaction and assembly occurs, and you see it distill water and medicines, then use any tool called «clepsedre», and its form is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads are passed through it by which the medicine cuts so that it stops well the urethra, so that it can be drawn out the moisture, and put back when necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and draw to the drawing which is outside; if you draw the moisture to the syringe, and then strongly close the drawing outside; the moisture will enter inside, and it will come to the bladder now, so that it can feel the pain; and this is the form of the subtle catheter with which one catheterizes the bladder: if it is in:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of lead, and is the highest of the joints; and it is removed from the shoulder where the tendons meet; then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you saw clustered in the bladder, then place it between the two breasts formed by a good piece of double woolen cloth, and heat the moisture above the fire; then pour the head of the clyster into the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder throughout the moisture, until the hairs feel that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then pull the string strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a bag, and put inside what you saw of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the methods of stone, and extraction together with remedies; and I have said the difference between the arrow embedded in rain, and all signs, and in which kind of stone one should open with a drill; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the arrow that is embedded in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder, similar to sharpness in its subtlety; and it opens wounds, and greatly increases the pain of the staff, and can many times, and then rots; and from many of these jumps the foundations; and it is light for the healing of children up to they are four years old, and is very painful in adults, and is constantly present, to those who are between young and old; and it is the cure less heavy of those who have the arrow large, than of those who have the small.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with a poultice, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand up and move it away from the body, so that the stone descends to the edge of the intestines, and never once rises above the thigh; then place it between your hands and cleanse it, with your hands away from your thighs, so that the intestines are completely declining downwards; then take and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If she does not chase the touchier douce away, then prick your middle finger of your right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your ring finger, if the pain is dull; and place it in the base, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the end with urine; then press against your finger, and the stone will come out where you see it was cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the urine into his hand, and command him to extend his right hand with the fingers in the air, and his left hand to remove the skin that is outside the fingers in the part where the incision is made; then cut the spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And between the bones and the foundation, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval; and the blade should be straight above the stone, and the handle should be attached or at the base, and the belly should be wide by default, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure that is at the base, that it should jump out without effort; and if there are parts where the stone has angles, and edges: if it is rough to get out; and if there is a part that is smooth, similar to a glass, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	When there are angles and margins in this place, make the incision larger; if it does not jump, then you must strain it with nails that are as thick as a lime at the head, to prevent the stone from escaping; or you can use a subtle hooked instrument at the head; and if you cannot engage it thus, enlarge the opening slightly, and if there is no decortication, then strain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then extract the small ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be made larger, and a larger wound should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the skin that the leeches cannot sew; but you must try to pull, or to tear with pincers, until you tear it into pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply enchantments of incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and put a moist linen cloth on top, in oil and wine, or in oil and vinegar and cold vinegar, to soothe the boil; then re-sew the wound over its collar, and do not leave the thread until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, rub the joint well with oil and vinegar, then apply a poultice of mustard plaster and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by the urine, which is known to be held back without a leak with the urine: then put your hand on the wound, and extract that blood, because if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and it will poison; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and baking soda, and help it in all ways that you can, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the ointments that you cure it with, that you bind them to both thighs, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is conducted with a stick, and tied with a thread, and the urine cannot issue; then the cure for this that I have said before, that you should cut many times, is to excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and be at three angles tied with a thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the rod outside the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently push the rod into the rod until it reaches the stone; and slowly turn the rod in your hand into the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if urine comes out immediately, then press your hand above what remains of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is currently broken, and has jumped with the urine, and is sharp to the limbs; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then remove the thread from the stone and the other from above, then make the rod in the place of the stone between the two pieces, then extract it forcefully, and remove the piece, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is hardly ever a stone in women, and if there is ever one, it is a difficult cure, and is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-trained who will expose herself to shame, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well versed in this hand skill; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is further forward than the man's, because of which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessary, she must be held down, and if you do not hold her down, do not do the operation; and present a wise woman well versed in women's affairs, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command for the examination of the stone; and look very carefully whether the woman is a virgin: therefore, it is necessary to put her on her back and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she must push it out of her body, and recommend that she lie on her back and press her right hand against her bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary to move it greatly from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut into the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone where it is musky and stained, and feel the arrow in that part; and do not move the other side above or below, and let the wound be small at first; then stop the bleeding by sewing in the belly, if you feel the arrow so sharp that the wound cannot be closed until the arrow can be removed, and know that there are many kinds of arrows: namely, small and large, sharp and blunt, long and round, and those with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you have similar cases to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you cannot see it, put the broken glass in your eye for an hour until the pain is gone; then return to your work, as long as the stone is not completely removed, and have the instruments that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone for men to help you in your work; if you cannot see it, and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on the eye and bandage it with tents and cotton, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, because it might kill the patient; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound has healed, then return to your work until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	For hernia, cause of cancer.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing other than the assembly of moisture or white sweat, which is outside the belly's curtain that contains the urine; and it is called «syfac», and never is properly in the web of the urine, if one wishes that it is another urine; and this is the skin of the belly between the white sweat that we have said; and it has no other.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this branch is due to its weakness that comes from the roots, and it is spread by that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the roots, and this moisture has many colors: it is a declining color to yellow, or no red, or black, or watery white, and there are more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, because if it is white and soft as we have said, it is the abscesses that we have said, it is short like the figure of an egg, and does not open the roots, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own skin, it is the abscesses that we have said with a part of the egg, and because of this people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the roots and the white softness, it feels good; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, try all the surrounding parts, for which form it has previously.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to as much power and the replenishment of its body; then place it on its back, on something a bit high, and cover it with much cloths; then bend over its left side, and command the minister to bend over its right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the kidneys; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the kidneys from the long one to above the knuckle, and make your incision straight in cutting the skin of the kidneys towards the white face, and scrape the subtle back according to as much power; then pierce the white plain with sharp and wide strokes, and extract all the sharpness, and then put your forceps, and close the white face above; and do not touch the kidneys except the white face itself; cover all or by pieces carefully the side of it subtly, that if you do not cover it well, it will return to the sharpness; and if the wound opens up in your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white face; then gather the two flaps of the kidneys at one seam, then cure it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you have to remove the corrupted flesh due to another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cover the wound with a suspended cloth, and remove the flesh, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the bone is assembled in two parts together, as it is two branches; then cover the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put some ground mullen in rose oil into the wound; and put another layer of ground mullen in wine and oil on top, and place two bandages over the two dressings, and tie it all together with a cloth according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and place them according to this likeness and be assembled by sewing in the neck of the undergarments, and one of the patient's arms over the foundation just above the back, and the other to the part of the wrist; and the other head above the two angles, and all together the restriction in the loop of the undergarment; and once this branch of the cautery is medicated in the shape of an iron tail, and it is that you take one cauterizing needle fine, and apply it to the skin of the wounds, and be heated as we have said, so that the white sap that contains the poison is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that sap with small incisions, and the scab with this subtle cauterizing:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And in all ways that you can, until you have extracted everything; and be careful that the knife does not touch the bone; and cleanse this work so that it is safer; and guard against bleeding, and avoid doing harm to the patient; and if anything goes wrong, such as an abscess or bleeding or other thing, treat it according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the pain is not severe, and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, then use perforation as I have told you; and when you are certain that water is the cause, sit the pain on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part away from everything, and put the perforation through the length of the body; and let the wounds be wide so that all the sharp edges flow out; then put cotton on the wound and tie it, and leave it to drain the remaining sharp edge; then treat the wound until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the sharp edge to escape from the wound mouth, then you must use a pen or the instrument that treats the sharp edges of hydropikes, as its form is as before; and enlarge the wound, and let the sharp edge return, and it will be assembled after six months or within a year, and when it is assembled as before, and so on, the pain will pass its days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscesses of the ears
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In the section of this branch, there are many positions that cause fear in many people, which seems to me to be better left alone; and I will tell you about the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from wounds, and also from the ears; and it is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excessive sharp and wet, which is spread in the ears, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the blood; and it does not have pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and perhaps some grayish, purulent, and yellowish abscesses, and of no color, and sometimes comes from a new out of an artery, or from inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from the artery, then it is known by the position of the abscess being high, when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of opening a vein are known by their position at the expression of gentle touching with your fingers, and can often make the cut above this similarity, and above others; and you should cover the wound with the curd of milk, then raise the wound up, and pull out the thread from the white surface, and deliver the suspended part of all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already sewn with these threads, then it is necessary that you cut the wound, and cover; and if it is in the surface, or inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all of that which is held, and cover it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the hair at birth is on the back of the head, it is necessary that you shave it all, and straighten the forehead, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then apply other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a type of abscess enclosed in an envelope resembling a blister, with the softening of the testicles, and the pain is great when moving; and the treatment of this disease is just as difficult and dangerous as the previous one, and we will tell you about its work, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to make the dislocated joint sit on its own seat, then lift the suspensory ligament of the tendons down to your fingers, and the ones close to the thigh, and tie them with the master knots, and extend them evenly; then cut the tendon with a wide blade at the cross point, until they are uncovered, and then scrape off all the parts, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then take an needle or doubled thread, and tie it to the first limb where the blood came from, and tie it to the other end; then cut them in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as we have said for others, so that no tendon is torn; because there is no harm, and if all the tendons come out, it is necessary to draw the tendons to all the tendons; so that he does not lose his grip through the incision of the tendons, and they dry and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are due to the section that comes out from the toothache, or the extension upwards on the belly in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that toothache to one of the coions; and this toothache is either from the section of it, or from the extension of it, and these two methods of many causes: from impact, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is the extension of the toothache, it is that it has little and little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal up to the front, because the toothache approaches the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs of the cutting of the tongue are that it brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and there are various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and it is for the end of the intestine and the heart because of the cutting of the tongue.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the misalignment, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron with fear, because it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of the work is that you command or misalign the intestine with your hand inside the wound, if it can be pulled back; then place the neck above and between your hands, and relieve the ribs; then place the key above, and cover all the skin of the incision with oil; then insert a finger in the lips of the belly according to what you have skill for opening the wound, and make sure that the two fingers do not come out; then scrape the tongue that is outside the skin of the incision, until the white tongue is completely exposed from all parts; then insert your index finger in the direction of the incision, between the white tongue that is outside the skin of the belly, and between the second tongue, and behind the belly, and between the second tongue; and move it gently with your right hand inside the skin of the incision, and place the white tongue in your left hand above, and relieve the belly over the white tongue; and command the minister to extend the belly upwards, and remove what is behind the flap; and if you find anything, bring it out of the stomach; then take a needle or a thread made of twelve threads of wool, and insert it in the back part of the tongue, which is after the skin of the incision; then cover the threads with oil, and tie them together in the shape of a cross, and bind the tongue, which we have said is outside the skin of the incision, with a strong thread of two parts; then cover the threads with oil, and tie them together in the form of two parts, so that none of the wool that grows can enter the wounds, that an abscess does not form; and finally place the first thread according to the first thread, and leave the tongue which is outside the skin of the incision as large as a finger; and then the other according to the roundness that the belly carries; then cover the part that is outside the skin of the incision, both without correction and with correction, and the bowels, as we have said before; then apply soft oil to the wounds, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white, pus-filled wound that we have said, after incision, due to doubt of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this has often happened, and let the arrow remain until it falls out of him; and if it takes too long to fall, then be sprinkled with hot vinegar, and put on what we have said, until it falls; then treat the wound with other treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to make the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made as the branch that is together with the viscera, in a similar way that you tie the vessels, after the tail lightly but firmly; then cover in, and treat the abscess of what works, until the vessels rot; and the treatment is as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
