Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes a rip or tear, as we have said, and open the wounds; and let no one touch the intestines with their fingers, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; and in any case, if it remains too long in this point, the pain or swelling increases, as we have said, because the intestines are stretched, then soften and inflate the wounds and open them; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have already said; and never is the cure done in this way: and it is that the wounds are squeezed on their back between your hands, then cover the wound of the tear with a large cloth according to the quantity of three fingers; and then remove the intestines that are outside the skin that covers them, then take the rag and place it on the wound of the tear; and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two wounds that appear from the tear above the head of the rag, and cut both; then remove the head of the rag, and do not cover the intestines or stretch them or do anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you remove the splinters, uncover and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The splinter is hidden, and does not appear in the rent, and the cauteries are dull in this limb, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of leather from harnesses
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of harnesses is softened in some people, because the chariots that are inside are mollified, and it can be seen; and when one wants to cure it, it is necessary to let the wound lie on its back, and to remove the softened leather from the natural leather; then bring together the two lips at a seam, and if you see that there is too much softened leather, cut it off at three or four seams tightly; then sew between the seams, and cure as with other wounds until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	for gently
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	It is customary in our law to speak gently, and because I wish not to speak of it in this book; and there are only two reasons for it: one is that the patient should respond gently when asked, and be treated gently; and the other is because we often have dealings with gently treating some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rabbits and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that gently is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we place the animal in hot water, until the hooves are softened and warm; then we take them in our hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the treatment of the tail: it is necessary to burn the beast, and press the skin of the intestines with your right hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and scrape over each vein at the top, when you have well burned them; and leave no trace of the superficial and subtle veins that are on the vessels; and this method of cauterization is better than that made by attraction, because by attraction something of the intestines may remain, by which the beast desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is according to the two ways that men are: one is that between the two testicles open as wide as the figure of a woman's nature, with hair, and sometimes cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has a penis like a finger and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of men and women is that you remove all the ingrown hairs and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine springs from the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the incision
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigen is a charred piece of wood placed on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have had it as big as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you clean the excess of the tentigen on your hand or in a basin, and wipe it lightly; and do not alter too much, because blood does not come, then the cure of other cures until it is healthy; and to another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use it, and by chance it jumps out, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called the old «cow disease».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to treat it, as we have said about the treatment, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of woman is not well perceived, or the perturbation is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to her; or it is caused by charms, or subtle or sharp sorcery, and it is made from within the marriage, or in the cost, or outside, or whatever it may be; and it prevents conception, and pregnancy, and possibly the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the look of the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears to be nearby, then it is either yours or his.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle facial swelling, and it is near the two lips, then hurry, and do as follows: bring your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two lips into a tube, until the subtle facial swelling is drawn out, and is over the swelling; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the limb, and massage the woman every day, so that she cannot sleep.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the facial swelling is hard and rough, then it is necessary to apply a poultice like a leaf of mint.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a horse's kick, lift it up and cover it with a cloth; and have remedies to staunch blood, such as acacia, bloodroot, incense, and an abundance of wheat flour; then apply a large piece of dry plaster, so that the wound does not suppurate; and thus let it remain, and cover it with a linen tent; then treat other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a horse's kick, cover it according to this method, unless it is an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the infected abscess in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids become old they become thelul; and we have had said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are formed in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, if not treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then the thelul with pincers, and the copper in its roots, then powder over medicines restraining blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then boil her feet for an hour, then put her in very cold water; and if there is discharge of blood, sit in a decoction of sumac and the skin of green pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take wheat flour, and mix with honey and egg, and make the poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If he is strong, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him lean back and apply suction cups to his back and breasts without injuring; then take the limb, and soak it in plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and apply suction to the joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the limb with poultices until it is healed; and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp chief, if it needs covering as I have said the thulium; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come in the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chaut abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary to say in this treatment of the chaut abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not one of the abscesses that collide; and if you know how to use iron, look at the abscess if it is agus at the beginning of its appearance, and plain of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, see if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce, but make him breathe so long as the pain is eased; and then place the painful part on a seat, and have two small seats where he leans, and rests on his back, and gathers his feet to the sides of the leg; and let his knees be spread, and put his arms outside his hips, and tie them well with a good belt; then apply the bandage towards the right side, and have the instrument ready that is used to open the mouth of the wound, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see the instrument being applied, that you first feel the depth of the wound, so that what enters into the instrument does not go further than it should, and that it does not harm the painful part; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument above, and stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When abscesses are open and they are squeezed out by hand, it should be covered with the head's chief, the spatula leath; and when the wound is empty, it should be put into the wound moistened tents in rose oil or green dry oil; and the tent far from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and above the marsh and above the other clean moistened gauze in hot water or boiled vinegar soaked; then after II hours of poulticing, as long as it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by a poultice of hot water and honey, and then of hot water or roots of lily and aristolochia boiled.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is sutured with a marl, it is necessary to be careful not to use iron, but to cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife is first to the birth that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman approaching, and wants to smell the ar: then the child quickly issues; therefore wash that child according to the natural figure, and it is its issue with its head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, if you should gently press his belly, so that the child comes out soon; for when it comes down on its head, and the second is with him, and it is washed with the marl of its superfluities by good cleansing; and this that comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because it never comes up from its feet, and comes out of the back or shoulder, and hands, or comes up over its belly, or sometimes, and is turned over its collar, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary for the bailiff to be wise and subtle in these things, and if he makes a mistake and is deceived, I will show you all the figures how one should help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of its head naturally, and the mother gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let the midwife sit on a seat, or let women hold her; and rub oil or fenugreek that has been cooked onto her back, and then give the bailiff a small spatula of this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second joint, and cover its angle as much as possible; and take the woman's belly so that the fetus descends, and if it does not, then you must clyster the woman with musk fenugreek powder with sesame oil; then let her swallow and spit out the mixture for an hour: then the fetus will now descend.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, then you must gently and gradually reset them; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and lift her legs up high; then remove the chair from the ground, and bend over the woman, so that she does not faint at the rising; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cover the hands with cloth that was previously placed on the belly, and extract the child, and reset it gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the child's birth above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes above its feet, it should be placed on its back; then gently turn it little by little until it is even; then grasp both feet and extend them gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up from the cradle, command it to lie down, and let it spit out its contents; if it jumps again, then God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not lie down as we have said, gently turn it little by little until it is in the natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be perfectly fine.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take a muscle sample from a high-quality, and oil of wormwood, and melted lead, and grind everything in a mortar; and put on the natural form of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright until above the ribs; and when she is softened out, make her a mirepoix, and put it out, and let her rest for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's head above its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place your hands gently and gently; then lean it on its neck, and hang its feet down, and lie it on the bed; then gently fold its hands, and grasp its arms from behind, until it is fully dressed below; and if the child does not cry, take its feet and move them gently, then move the stomach upwards, then push your hands; and gradually feed the child little by little; and command the woman to hold it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out widely with a hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then lift the woman and go; if she cannot go, then make her lie on the bed, and bend her legs; then apply the muscle relaxation that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then study how to bring back the hand; and when the child is born, place it according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command that it be pinched until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's neck, and have his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	it is necessary that the midwife wash his hand, then turn it slowly and gently; when it is aligned, place the muscle-like substance of butter and oil on it, as we have said, then command her to move it slowly; when you have done this, place it on a chair, and command her to sit; and make him spit
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all the second joints
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	when he comes to do this for all the second joints, hold the second joint against your finger, until the moisture is removed; and if the child cries out from his face and neck, hold it against its back, so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then give the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to sit only once: then it is gently released
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is not uncommon for twins to be born many times, and sometimes three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, if not for the cord that ties them together, which is attached to the belly; and sometimes they are born as naturally as one at a time, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born forcefully, as we have said the care should be, and if the afterbirth is subtle, and she does what it does quickly and lightly, then do so as it is good for her health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, or seventh month, and are all formed into the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise one, and it is best that the baby swallow everything, because by chance similar things happen to them; so do as it should be.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When treating the woman of the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to use manuals; if the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death; then it is best that she lie on her back, and her arms are inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the minister gives two parts of tansy, or she is left lying in bed if she is not treated for the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the woman with moist cloths with mustard and fenugreek and seed of lin, then put her hands in these oils and mustards; then give her lightly, then let her drink whatever is convenient to her, and if the child is born take care that it descends above its head; if it is born with its eyes open put it in her arms or on her chest or in her mouth or in some palace or behind the beard or under the chin or in the middle of the ribs; and if it is born with its eyes closed put it in her arms or on her shoulder or in the middle of the ribs; and it is best that she ties the umbilical cord to her right hand, and puts the cauterizer between her left hand fingers, and gives a light blow to all her hand, and puts the umbilical cord in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the umbilical cord:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place the other finger against it, where you have the skill, so that the extraction is even; and then move it back and forth, to make it come out, and hold the teeth together, as it is in this form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, then use one of its two fingers, and push it into that part, and remove the other part; and if none remains, then place this finger or a higher one on the joint, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by pressure, then you must wrap it over the injured part, until it all comes out; then place it in the joint of the foot or at the heel, and so you must do in the other hand, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the question is about a child who is large and has a sharp point at the end, it is necessary to drive the spinal process between your fingers and make the head and extract the sharpness; or you break it with the tool called «almidach», from which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and thus the same is done for a child with a great natural head; and then pull out the bones with pliers, and if the question is about a child who jumps up and down, hold him tightly to the forceps, if they are broken, until the blood issues forth; and if it cannot issue, cover it with pieces of cloth that you can; and if it is inflated in the belly or outside the ribs, it is necessary to pierce it so that the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If it is above its feet, then it is light attraction, and the direction to the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stiff in the abdomen or the groin, it is advisable to extract it with a cloth wrapped around your hand; and when the abdomen or groin, as long as the moisture that is there; and if the other member is broken, and the patient remains, then lift the hand from the marsh, and drag it to the mouth of the marsh; then pull out one or two, and remove it; and if the mouth of the marsh is retracted due to an abscess that has come, it does not matter to struggle, but it is advisable to administer moist and greasy things; and the medicines are plasters, and they are in high softening and moisturizing and greasing.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it back in place, as we have mentioned in the living child; and if you cannot do so, then break the limb into pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And once you have done that, as we have mentioned in the abscess chapter; and if blood comes out, it should be strictly bandaged, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted the other with regard to that one, and it also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the groin, and they swelled so much that they burst, and then began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the doctor, and he thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied strong adhesive, and it pulled out some bones, and after some time, others came out.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in it were many bones, until the woman was much better; and she saw the woman thus for a long time, and it was stuck with a little blood from the body; and I had not remembered this chapter before because when masters find an unusual thing, they do not know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marble back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of pressure, with which we open the books; and to the second returns to the second questions of the two joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	All the same, the corners should be more subtle than the restraint, and made of flat or boxwood; and the mouth of the fust should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees should be one palm and a half; and in the two limbs should be two adjustments of this same fist, which should be firm in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marble when returning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of flat iron or boxwood, according to the appearance of needles; and it should have two prongs, as you see, one palm long, and two wide; and when you want to open the wound all at once with the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet together and her legs spread, then push the two prongs together into the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her breasts; then work your hand with the instrument equally, according to the quantity you want to open the mouth of the wound, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This tool is surrounded by many similar ones; and when the one you have matched is ready, the work is faster, and higher in quality for its quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not disregard the tool that you have not matched, for its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second one is held in childbirth, it is necessary to command the patient to hold his tongue, and then let him spit out the conditions, and hold your hands to his mouth and nose; and if he sneezes through it, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the pot, and make a sneeze or covering, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as wormwood, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled or potent over the fire; then put a spoonful or sneeze of pot in the mouth of the marsh, and the other chief in the mouth of the marsh, and let it steam until the vapors come into the mouth; then make him spit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient sneezes repeatedly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and is not better, command the midwife to moisten her right hand with sesame oil or mustard plaster, and then rub it into the skin, and repeat the second treatment; when she finds it, grasp and stretch it gently and straight, so that the husband does not prevent its extraction; but move it slightly to the right and left, and then remove it; it will come out and disappear.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is too narrow, we have said the cure of vomiting and fumigation of herbs; and if she is not of all that we have said, keep in mind that you do not force to draw; but it is good that what is at the mouth of the womb, you tie to the belly of the woman, then counteract with tetrefarmon ointment; if it will pass and be returned, and she will be well; but anyway, when she passes if there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and bleeds the pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then apply contraversial fumes to the head: none of the ancients have experienced the fume of willow and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to fume the woman during retention of flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like glass in shape, and one places the head subtly into the nature, and the others wide over the fire; and let the fumes be over the charcoal, and the tine until it is wasted, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but it has been stopped by some subtle sphincter: therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that sphincter at its proper place, and not to pierce any space agut, and to cover the location so that it does not touch; then put on a moistened cloth with wine and oil, then the treatment of the wound until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not set, place or press a splint on it, and let it remain for some time, and it should be strengthened as the child wishes to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this swelling of a wound or an abscess; if it covers the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the base
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the base are nodulation, and thicker than those that come above the base, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodulation is old, it works, and contracts moisture to become white or subtle bone, and never are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosities when the pain makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate the middle of the penis; and they reach the joint of the hip, and perforate out of the buttocks.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you make your two fingers or basement, and put a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you put a thin tent of cloth, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or the hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no perforation, egestion, or windiness, as we have said: cut so that it does not perforate more; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near a urine conduit, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the joint of the knee, and the tendon is close to the bone; if there is no twisting and the location of the pain is not clear, then it is likely that it is attached, and there is no cure by medicine or lancing; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no other cure than labor, and the vanity of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, in the hope of healing by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the pain is hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are raised up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then place a tin or lead plate, if there is twisting, until you remove the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you must apply your two fingers, so that it seems to have pierced the sac; and if you feel between your thumb and index finger, then cut it out; since there is no other way to heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can indeed heal some, but this rarely happens; and the aid that is made, is to heat the fine cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and push everything out through the fistula, until it reaches beyond the base; and do this two or three times, until you see that these shreds are removed, which are similar to a barbed arrowhead; then treat the wound with moistened burdock, as long as those shreds are removed, then treat the wound with ointment and bandage.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If otherwise, nothing else can be healthy; and if it is between two, and does not pierce just at the base where it is founded, and between your thumb and the tent there is a thick covering of char or syfac, and you see the fistula pointing towards the covering of the cure; if the copper of the beginning of the fistula, and before the tent, and then the cauterize after, until it comes to the top of the tent; and it will be delivered from the tent, and closed; then cleanse those char that seem like a quill of an eagle, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot pull it out, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization does two things: it burns away the charred flesh and stops the bleeding of blood and removes moisture; then cure tents made of butter or of bruised herbs until the wound is healed, and the charred flesh is drawn out into the wound; then cure the wound with dry ointments made of hard charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is healed, it is healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from just above the foundation, and is distant from the body, then press on the top or foundation, and ask what it is.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there is thread or sutures or charcoal where it is about to pierce, if there are no other means but hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it just above the foundation, or if you can put tents and cure it as we have said; do not move too much in front, so that you do not cover the foundation that holds the base, and bring the egestions through the way you want; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and uncover it when it is cut below the foundation, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then clean the char that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to keep the fistula in the part before the foundation: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And often, fistulas are made in this way: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, it is where it is connected to the base of the skin on top of the flesh, so take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push the wire through it, and push the probe along the entire length of the wire into the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not found at the edge of the base inside, then push the wire from that perforated one, so you push your other end to the bottom; and take the top of the wire, and put together the two prongs together, and hold them against each other, and leave it there for a while, until the thread covers those charred parts that are between the two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then try to puncture it in all possible ways that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not matter to make the sutures so deep if it is too deep, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous spur that is made for the fistula is very sharp and pointed; on one side it is sharp and cutting; and on the other part, not, because we do not know what we should not do, as you see there.
des emorroydes	from the worms
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Worms are in two ways: either they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood inside them, and some have a little or a lot of blood, and some have no blood at all, and some have blood in their roots. The treatment of those that are within the foundation is that you command the patient to urinate in other rooms until the foundation is clean, and then you remove them with tweezers, or with your fingernail, then you cut off their roots; if they cannot be held by their moisture, take them with a needle, or cotton, or a piece of cloth; then stretch them out, then cut them off, and powder over some hot powders that are in the cauterizing chapter, or cauterize them as it is said, or in the cauterizing chapter, and treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot come out, then clean the wound with a sharp and rough clyster to remove what is inside the foundation, so that it can come out openly; and if the wounds are closed, and the filaments are strong from the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you hold them with your fingernail or with tweezers, then cut them off, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and do not make an incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to suture the wound according to this method: take a thread of twisted wool, and tie it into a needle, then pull the thread upwards and pierce the needle from the other side, and bring the two ends of the thread out on either side of the needle, and make it wide; and straighten the thread evenly, then untie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood out; then put under the wound a cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and put under the wound, and command the patient to rest; and then let him rest until they heal, and when they are healed, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	drily with the hands where the base is founded
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often found dry where the intestines are, and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to shave at the point of a scalpel or with your fingernail above, which does not let it moisten; then treat it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be dried, then start the shaving stronger than before, until it is fully healed, and then shave; then treat it as it should be while it is healed.
dou fremit	high fever
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Mouse is a small appearance deformed at the chest, and it goes up a lot in front; and sometimes the true one finds the frost, and the smell is like that of death from fever, and it comes to all the body, and more than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose, or a pen of vulture very strong, and put that quill on the fever, as long as the circle surrounds the fever all around; then turn your hand to the whole quill until you cover all around the fever, and put it in front, and extract the fever from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this in the form of a rain or iron dog according to this shape, and be subtlely removed and drawn upwards:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not make a mistake, to hold it in the two places and press it; and if you see, cauterize the pain, as it is before or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the splint
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a splint of silver or bronze, or iron melted or woven; and never make one of these small and large instruments according to those with which they are equipped.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are to be nursed in the care of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the bandage is small and large, depending on how wide the belly is tied in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a deficiency where the belly is tied, as you see, and the cloth is inside perforated; and at one side it has two holes, and at the other one; and the belly or put medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is perforated all around with small holes, and there is between each hole one inch of space, then sew in these holes with strong thread twisted in X or around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument before a strong thread, then bandage; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the poultice with oil or honey or something similar, then press it lightly; then the nurse gives it to the patient's two hands together, until it is all soft, then remove the poultice, and relieves the pain in his legs at once, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice in the illness of diarrhea, and the medicine wants to come out, start it again as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if they are morbidly swollen at the base, or in an abscess, then the poultice should be as delicate as for a child; and this is the form of the delicate poultice with which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the parts or wounds that are made, and from which they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are made from the sharpness of a spear, and the size of a sword or a dagger, or a lance or a staff or a sieve, or similar things; or they are made according to the length of the body, such as a wound that pierces through the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because its chapter is remembered.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from sharpness or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt the development of an abscess: if you bandage it immediately from the cephalic itself if it comes soon with blood from the wound, and the bandaging should be on the opposite side of the injured part; and avoid the painful repletion of wine and heavy food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the patient does not want to be treated, if he refuses, then his meat should be weakened, and he should not drink wine, nor change his food; and he should put on the wound, if there is an abscess that comes, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in sterilizing wine; and if there is no abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if his arms have moved it, then put on some ointments, as long as he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a tailor's cut and similar, and the lips cannot come together by tenting, then stitch them together by sewing, as I will say about wounds of the belly, from sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and can, but does not hold except at one point if it is sutured; then treat the wound with medicine, and apply a hard char in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large amounts of food, such as tests and cooked grain, like chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you tear or perforate the skin, and it does not reach to the bone, then suture the entire wound, and pour out pus, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting it, and it cannot be stanched by medicines, then ligature the artery, and if you tear it, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put this powder that boils like the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take a part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; fresh chalk three parts, and the powder finely, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins with all its own blood; then bind it firmly, and leave it without movement, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never use chalk alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but that the wound has moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound moves, immediately apply this powder; but put on top some ointments, or flour of oats made with honey and water, until it becomes soft; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the broken bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the main fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main fractures, but if the neck nerves or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other method than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, because it hurts bones and makes them retract; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and its continuity is with the brain, which is one of the highest members; but let the medicine be gentle, as calcium washed in hot sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the bandage washed also in hot sweet water, and other stones of this kind according to this manner, and moist warm compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with a bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
