Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and the bone is exposed and full of pus, then drill or go deeper into the bone; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then stop it, and tie it, and cauterize the wound as necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the ribs, and the lung is exposed, keep it away from the food that goes down, and do not touch the neck but return it to its natural shape; then gradually tighten it, and leave it for some time, then cure the wounds until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, try to remove all of them, and those that you cannot remove, leave them until the wound heals, and is aligned and cleaned of any pus.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of spear or of dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or dagger, and the wound is deep, look to see if the hairs on the wound are singed: cut away then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh at all its blood, do not put in the first hour the powder, nor tie it with a bandage for the blood so that it does not clot immediately, and return to the heart, and oil the pain; but put on an attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put in the wound old cotton to draw out the moisture, and let the pain sleep over the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor trembling of the heart from elsewhere; and when you see the good dispositions, cut away that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of tents and other treatments, as long as they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and work, then there is a fistula; if the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword cut, and it is simple, or at the front or back, then the treatment of what is in front; if it is large, stitching; and if it is small, powder, and if it is embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, then remove the pieces from the wound, and the threads if they are not decayed; and if they are not decayed, let the wound rot, so that the extractions are not harmed; and for other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	abdominal rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	1. The rupture of the abdomen is large and medium and small; from the great wound, once the intestines or the nerves of the intestines, by which the infiltration of them; and the suture is more painful, and once the small wound is worse than the great one, because one must put the intestines back, if not put them back in their place; because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, then put them back more carefully, and because the medium-sized wound is worth less, because one must mend the intestines to their place as with other ones II And there are four ways that the rupture of the abdomen is according to: the two common sutures are in the suture of the abdomen, and the suture of the other wounds of the body and two other sutures proper are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more proper with the suture of the abdomen, and I will say one by one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the inside is forced out, and it is easy to put back, it is done by one of the two methods: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflated by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a handful of dry cloth, or cook it in boiling water and vinegar and salt, and roll the intestine until it is softened; and never do this with restraining force, and it is better to let it cool to avoid injury.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, if the intestines are moist from sharp or high and misshapen things, because by this they are aligned and enter quickly; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision with the instrument used to remove foreign bodies; and the first care is to stop the bleeding, as we do not cut without great necessity. And this is the tool for cutting: slice from within the belly and outside, and cut through the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines have jumped out, if you can put them back in their natural form according to their own place, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the part outside of the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part outside of the belly, put the head and the worst part higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is at hand, then place your hands between the wound and put the painful parts together; this is the common way of stitching, and you should use needles or several, depending on the size of the wound, leaving a space of two fingers' width from the edge of the wound, and then thread a needle with strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the needle, which is outside the skin, until you make it pierce through that part, and bring together the two ends of the needle four times; then wind the thread around the needle twice, and evenly stitch the wound, leaving a space of two fingers' width, and then thread another needle; and tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this until the whole wound is stitched; and the needles should be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cover the entire wound, and thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason, they should be medium-sized; and do not place the needles too far from the skin and flesh, so that they do not cut the wound before the sewing; and then cover the ends of the needles with bandages or cloth to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sewn; this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one needle or two: when you have pierced these parts together, pull the needle to the part where you started, as if you were drawing a thread; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a finger.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been for 24 hours missing, and the wound was dressed with 15 hours, and cured, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother had thought that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines; and I put wet cotton twice a day over the wound, and washed it with vinegar until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle and the thread from the inside to the outside; when it has pierced the right through the right, place the head of the suture or stitch where you have inserted the needle, and pierce it from the other side of the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier makes the furs, and leave one end of the suture once, and take it up again from the other side, until the sewing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the main needles to the other head, in this manner: stick a needle or main needle close to the wounded part, and make it pierce only that one alone, and leave the two wounds; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part inside, the two wounds, then pierce both from the front part inside, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the easiest way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If this is said by a woman, and no one testifies against it, then the stomach should be sewn with two needles, or one in each; and one needle should be inserted from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corroies; and sucked that when the rupture is in the stomach, it is sewn more painfully than other stitches of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like that of other wounds: and it is that when you remove the fresh wound completely, as soon as the art has moved it, you reset the intestine and the skin; then put on the powder mixed with char, and if the art has moved it, put on any ointment present until the wound heals; and bind the bandage, and be sure of the sifac and the mirror; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on cotton cloth immediately when it begins to bleed, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For in many positions of wounds that are simple, and if you doubt whether the wound does not communicate with principal members, then it is necessary to make a light mollification around the angles, and on the joints; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and often happens, then clysterize with black wine, and immediately if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and perforate within, and cut out what is inside, as for the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is exposed, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to the nature of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the splinter jumps out of the wound, put it back in place as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned black, then you must tie the part that has turned black, so that blood does not come between, for there are veins and arteries; then cover what is between the limbs, and put the two needles hanging from the part away from the wound, to align the extraction when the splinter breaks, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the breakage of the bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured, and the wound is small, it can be restored to some people, because I saw that one man was gutted by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and was inflamed and became a fistula, and inside were feces and vomit; I put care according to what I knew, and did not stop until it was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewing, I doubted that the hairs had no harm in his belly; but there was no harm, only he remained in better positions, and changing and drinking; and the experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he should be bound in this way: take warm baths, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the warmth has opened the mouth, put it over the two lips, so that it holds his mouth closed; then cover the wound, and hold it in such a way that he cannot dislodge it, then apply the other warmth in this way as before, until the wound is completely healed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief of the shoulder is burned inside, and no harm comes to the hairs, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thin thread, then pull the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back into the hole; and this method of stitching is only as far as the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no remedy or cure, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	all wounds or abscesses, when they appear, are universally called "fistulas", and specifically when they are cut and opened.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to its hard and white, dry, and where there is no pain, and it is cut as a pen quill; and sometimes it is clear and thick; sometimes small and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, except by one of the EIGHT causes: that is, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hard pus inside and on the lips, which does not allow new pus to form; or there is too much pus; or the eyes are swollen, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is in the manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and late health, and flows by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of fistulas made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to great veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the main member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are of great discomfort, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the joint that I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, if it is straight, take a tin or iron tent, and if it is curved, take a subtle tent of cloth, for the cloth plies around the twist; and if the fistula is perforated and you cannot well encircle it by tents, then cauterize one of the perforations, for the moisture does not come out from one perforation to another, and cleanses it; then carefully apply it to your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is deep in the joint, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the location where he feels it; and when you will truly know the location where it is, and whether it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then treat according to what I have told you, and remove the faulty part and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then treat until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep at the right place, then cut it open as much as you can, then put moistened tents in medicine water, and pour them into the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous part that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments with clean cloth, as long as they are healed; and if they are not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then treat.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not cause harm to your principal limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove the corruption until it is completely removed, then cure the things injured by the tooth as long as they are healthy; and if they are not healthy, and remain bowed as before, cut off that part which you have already removed: if it reveals and wishes to come out as far as you can reach, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, then it is too deep in the bone, and you cannot reach it; there is no other method except to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pincers, then remove it with the appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, then take them all out, and do not leave any behind; and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then treat and moisten and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something soothing on the wound, and leave it until the flesh is completely surrounding the bone, and then the bones will be lighter; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, if the corruption has spread so much that the bone is completely rotten, then cover the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption that comes close to the bone; if it should be and cover all around the corruption, and then cure it until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	When the young man was around 30 years old, he had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it was filled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctor by their folly opened it so high that the abscess opened, and there were many matters coming out, and became a fistula, and there was much pain that everyone was groaning and moisture in the body; and many doctors treated him within two years, and there was no cure in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and what was coming through the fistula to the great body; and his body became red like the young man, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that one was coming into contact with the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then stretched out my hand into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from inside; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and I thought there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with various medicines for a long time, but could not heal it; then I returned and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then I removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb; but I could only wrap around a palm of the bone and treat it entirely, then I applied medicines; and it became healthy and healed quickly, and did not require any further treatment except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was healed entirely, and in place of the bone grew a hard cartilage, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction throughout, neither to the left nor to the right.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a bandage, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it be extended upwards; and place another bandage of thicker material than the first bandage, above the cartilage that is on top of the bone, and extend the head, so that you can remove the rotten cartilage from below, and uncover the cartilage above the part where you see it should be, so that it does not rot; and place a poultice or a bandage outside the bone to cover the rotten cartilage; and it should be done in such a way that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the tooth is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, remove the tissue completely; then put on the bandage from one part to the other, and sew the corruption, and let the stitch be as long as possible, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cover the joint with the corrupted part, and sew the bone or the part it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cover; and if the corruption is at the tip of the hand or the foot, it is very difficult, but nevertheless you should inquire about that corrosion, how it opens; and cleanse it in all ways possible, but do not let the vein or the nerve do harm; and know that the instruments for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore you should arrange each kind of work with its corresponding tool; and know that the work will show you the tool you have to use, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool you have to use according to what it is suitable for.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The members will rot either due to the lack of nourishment or due to lack of strength; and when you have cured that corrosion by the medicine of the cures, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain escapes through the mouth or by the malice, which is greater, of the lack of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and becomes blacker afterwards, as those corrosions of members spread from one to another, and take hold of the whole body; if you hasten to cover, and if it is due to the sting of some poisonous animals, such as scorpions of the sea and snakes and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the hand, then cover and do not give them any space to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, if the cope is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cope at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do as the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, if the cope after the other joint; and if it comes where the pain is, if the cope all the pain; and if it goes up the leg, if the cope at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than the patient lies on his back and the assistants hold one end of the limb, and the other assistants hold the other end of the limb, and they dry the char between the two limbs to the span wide, until the bone is revealed; then the cope or cloth, and put a piece of linen on each part so that the cloth does not touch the uninjured skin, and it comes to other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding comes when you are working, cauterize the wound quickly, or apply some powders that stop the bleeding; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bandage the injured limb with a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in great pain: he had a wound that looked like burning by fire, and that corrosion first came to his right side, taking over the whole side; and when the honorable man saw the corrosion, he covered the wound, and was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion came again from the other side of the hand, and it came to me, and I put things on after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I would cut off his hand, and I would not, because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and he also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he gave up all hope, and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I have not told this except for the reason that one should do something else if one has such a matter.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never does an abscess form in a wound that is not properly cleaned, and it remains for such a long time that it causes a great collection of pus; then it bursts and drains, and the pus jumps out, and the wound remains open like a wound that has not healed, and the skin above is also as thin as cloth and does not adhere to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called "sinus", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from the front, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cover all of it with cloth, and immediately when it is thin, as if it were cloth; and it does not remain for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin is hardened and the corruption is not yet in full force, and the skin is charred, then use this ointment for healing: look to see if the breasts are large, and the nipples have a foul odor, then make an Egyptian-style ointment as follows: take equal parts of aloe, oil, and litargyr, mix them with heat in a vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take according to your need, and make it into a thin and thick paste, and apply the ointment to the breasts, and hold the nipple; leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by sprinkling; do this many times until the breasts are clean and healed; if the pain is too great, and the Egyptian ointment and water ash do not help, then apply an ointment of water and honey or a little litargyr broken up; or use an ointment of honey and wine melted, which has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the skin soft; when you have done this, and you are sure the breasts are clean, then apply an ointment made of rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments, as I have described their properties for treating wounds; if the nipple of the breast is small, and the ointment cannot enter, then enlarge it with a small needle, and put in an Egyptian-style tent of the ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is large enough to enter; if the wound is too large, then leave it alone, and let the skin or lower part of the breast where the ointment can enter, and if the nipple that is above is also foul, then cover it with a cloth.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement. Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest is pushed inward after many hours, push the chest back so it does not remain misaligned.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elbow
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the elbow due to a pouch of the hand, or a pimple, or by chance in other places; and when it is drained, and one does not take care, if the abscess comes back, and they continue to pour boiling water until it reaches the root of the elbow, and perhaps it reaches the whole; and then there are corrosions just above the bone, as long as there is pain, and the patient has two large wounds, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, then you must remove all the excess that remains from the elbow, then cauterize the wound afterward.

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The sharp pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The sharp pain that arises in the hands of some men by chance is all chronic, and sometimes it is in the fingers or where there are bones, and never in the nail, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or in any of the ten fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile. des vils	of the base
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large and swollen with excess melancholy, which come in many members of the body; and more so in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should never administer any purgative of clay, and then give the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron is in two ways: one is that you apply it, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein, and draw out all the blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tail is done in this way: first, the first leg of high hot water very strong, until the big without being subtly removed, then straighten the leg with the bad from above the hip to the part below the groin; then cut the vein in the thigh, or in II or III, of a wide incision, then release and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, until as much blood can be suffered by the bad from the leg; and then tie it, and command that he boil meat infusion with black pepper; and repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and not bent to the bad.

Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit. de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is opened in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land; and by chance it opens elsewhere than in the legs, and this has to do with the porridge that comes out of the skin, as it comes from within the body serpents and worms, opened between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that it comes in the leg a very large inflammation, then the limb changes, and the vein begins to issue forth, like the root of a plant.

When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth of one and a half inches wide and long enough to cover the limb, and tie the cloth, leaving the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not attached to the limb, if you wrap it around the cloth, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover its root until it is all out; for if you cover it, it will return to the vein, and cause abscess and rot in the limb, and severe disease; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little from the top, and nothing remains or corrupts; and this vein never occurs when it is treated with herbs of length one palm or ten, and some have come to me, which issued from ten palms in length, and when you cover it, it will burst the skin or puncture, and perforate it from bottom to top, so that everything comes out; and let the matter that is inside be drained, and administer medicines for rot every day, then cure as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein, it does not rain, and especially when it opens in the joint of the little finger, or the big toe, and there is much pressure, and from which it can rain; therefore, as we have said before, cure it accordingly.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of verses that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, ascending and descending, and is felt well in each member to member, until it reaches the skin where it went, and jumps out; and it is caused by some humors, such as come vers and serpents and lumbrics and ascarides or intestines; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the brain, perhaps entering, and destroys the brain; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the patient and treat them, it is necessary that you hold the limb above and away from a very tightly bound place, then cut across and pull it out, and if it turns in front of the char, you do not remove it, but cauterize with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it spreads oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or approaching near the oil, hold it away from it firmly, then cut across and pull it out; and it is necessary to use the remedy of wound healing of corpses of medicines dissolved for the bad humors caused by diseases, and if it becomes swollen with indigestible food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "windiness", and it is a pain that comes in some members, and it moves from member to member; and I see what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed to me one of her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise as high as a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything, like live silver when it cuts through flesh; the pain departed from that arm, and went into the shoulder, and then a little later it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she turned around inside the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease move in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had heard that it could move from one limb to another, but I had not seen it do so in this way; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, and because that constraint appeared; and it did not appear in this way to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease and the pain it causes, if it appears as we have said, then hold the limb above and below quickly, and then cover it with a cloth until that constraint is released from the limb; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat the cause of that constraint, such as fetid pills, and serpentine pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the types of bodies they penetrate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is such that there are arrows with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and sharp; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and the one that pierces any member as it pleases: whether in a principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it pierces any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, is apparent: then you must proceed with the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many ways; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely out, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the skull when the arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and the spasm that is above the skull, are squinting and swelling and vertigo and dizziness, and inflammation and dizziness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without force of the nose, or of the ears; and perhaps paralysis of speech and voice; and the spasm of the wound with moisture white like chicken, and also like boiling oil; and if these signs appear to you, then take care of the patient, and remove the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the arrowhead is about to enter or exit, it is near the right breast, and it feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not moving; and perhaps the arrowhead moves like a chicken's beak, and there is black blood, and cold sweat, and syncope: therefore, without doubt, the patient dies.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has not been pulled out is that without complaining of pus, it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limbs change color, and it gasps for breath and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the roof of the mouth, it is below the small ribs; and it causes great pain and difficulty breathing; and they move all the member of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the stomach, by chance if it jumps out of the wound nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the abdomen, and it does not come out through the intestinal wall, there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bladder, and the urine comes out and flows out, and the pain is very great: cut open the wound as it is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and back and spine and hip and knee and feet, and similar members, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow hit him in the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and took it out from the other side of the ear grease, and he was healed without any trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And there was a young man who had an arrow in his fat outside the paper, and the arrow was inserted, and he could not reach it except for the tip facing forward, and the arrow was long like a Turkish bow, all of it was made of iron without ears; the wound was healed, and no bad accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there was an arrow in the neck of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I shaved the beard, and subtly removed it until I removed it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was an arrow in a man, which was in his head or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut into the wound, and probed it, and removed it, and there were no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you want to help someone who has an arrow stuck in their back or shoulder, and the wound was closed over it; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor found harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And another man, who had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was closed over it; and it remained like that, suffering great pain; and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow was shot at the man of the prince, the king, who had it in his neck, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely inserted, I was called to cure after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a thin tent to it, and I did not feel anything; but he felt a sharp pain and discomfort on the right side of his ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow sticking out; I applied a poultice of attractive digestive herbs to it because the wounds were not inflamed, and then I saw the arrow's point.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice again, and immediately closed the wound, and then he felt the arrow's point long and tense, as if it were inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed medicine of corrosive acid on the wound by hand, as long as it was open, and tried to remove it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead which remained in the flesh; then I applied more medicine of corrosive acid into the opening of the wound, until the arrowhead appeared visibly; and it passed well through the ends within four months, and then began to decay if the wound that I had put nails on one side and the other, and could not get out; therefore, I did not cease to subtilize and engineer in various ways of instruments, until I got a good nail on a day, according to what its form would be at the end of this chapter, as long as I pulled it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the nasal cartilage could not be restored: I restored it then, and it was dressed with the wound, and the pain was healed entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you may place your care where I do not say, for the books cannot contain all; but the wise masters know well a great many things, and what is present and lacking, find nine works, and nine instruments, in the understanding of things strange that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the members except in two ways: either by the way they enter, or by another part; and that which sails through the way it enters, is an arrow entering into its flesh, and has never been out once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, let her stay until the charcoal is fully cooked and ready to issue; and also if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot get out, let her stay thus for some time, and move her every day; and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, then perforate around all the forest subtly, until the bones inside are widened, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the bellies of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not remove it, but let her stay until it is even after some time, for if the arrow comes towards the face, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not firmly lodged in the bone only, and does not come out by itself, and stays for several days without causing harm, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply lodged and cannot be pulled out, then apply tar as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healed.
