Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is in the body and cannot be seen, then apply tar to the entire wound; and if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then leave it until the wound is large enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place, then carefully remove the char that is firmly attached to both sides of the wound as much as you can, and then break or crush the ears of the arrow until you can remove it; and be careful not to break the arrow when removing it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then push the lung back inside through the ribs, as extraction causes pain.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding from the vein makes it difficult for you, follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and guard against cutting into the nerve and the vein, and use caution as you draw out the arrow without danger, or quickly or firmly or tightly; and put the painful part according to the form it was in when the arrow fell off, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do so, follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place where one can see or feel it: cut then above, as much as the hooks can take, and then extract it: if it has now burst.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone until it enters, then expand the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if there is arrow shaft left, give it all at once; and if it is sharp, and you are administering it gently, if you administer the instrument with a hair, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then give it all at once, and if the arrow is pulled out, pull the instrument in entering, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all of the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is stuck in the chest or abdomen or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cut through, then cover it if you can; do not cut into the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then treat the wound if necessary; and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the beak of a bird, to stick into the point of the arrow, such as this shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs to stick and to hold is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins that can be opened, of which 16 have heads, namely: two that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples apparent; and the two veins that are in the arm pits of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the front; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two nerves that are on the neck; and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the two veins outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins that are usually cut are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the right side, and it is called "the great vein"; and the middle one is called "the basilic", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and it is called "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the left side, and it is called "the vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and it is that one which is usually cut, which opens clearly above the fossa.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the auricular and annular, and it is on the right arm; and in the leg and where the foot is, there are three veins: one is outside the corbeure of the left side costeit, and the second is at the knee of the right side costeit; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is at the knee of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	For the shoulder joint, which is after the ears, helps with ancient enemas and migraines; and the quality of the sauna, as I tell you, and is that you remove the head of the pain, and rub the skin where the ears are on a rough cloth; then strangle the pains neck to a rope, until the two ears appear behind the ears in two directions from the head: then give it to your hand, and where you feel the hair of your hand, if it is sore; then take the lancet, and push it out of the ear towards the bone, then lift your hand to the whole ear above, and scrape and the skin and the ear well it should be through the traversing, and make the blood come out until you see; then strain and tie, as long as it is healthy; and I have already said the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The first line translates to: "For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sain of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the sain of the cerebral diseases of the face, headache, and rheum; and the quality is such that the pain is strange, twisting the neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called «fosseur», which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then release the neck from the pain, and tie the vein until it is healed and never again with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	It does not matter whether the flames are too sharp or not, and the cut should be across, because the bone is close, and by chance it may break the flames when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The cutting of the two veins that are in the two arms helps to those at the elbow, and at the wrist, and at the root, and at the eye in the oil, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their cut is such that the pain is strained by twisting any limb, as before; then the cut, and let the cut be across, a little long with the flame, a little wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the flames are thin, perhaps it will break; then correct the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie it with thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the nose is not good for a headache and fever, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and headaches that come in the face, and always when it is old; and the quality of the vein is that the pain is strained on its neck, then strain its nose to your right hand, and take the thin flame long, and put it on the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not move too much in front, and correct the blood according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is soon restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the second kind helps to narrow the alainne, and at the beginning of the meselerie, and with many diseases, and with empetigine, and with corrosions, and with herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the salve is such that the pains strangely pull away from one and the other, as we have said; and so the masters are above the chief of the pains, and the pains sit on one seat, then clean the vein with a long one slightly wide, then drain the blood promptly, or as much as the matter requires; then make another in the other vein, then release the limb, and hold the veins evenly, so that the pains do not strangle; and let it rest until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the liver above helps to cool in the mouth, and prevents tooth decay, and cracks in the lips, and mouth sores and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the pain disappear in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at both the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore match both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then match the largest of each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disorder
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The disorder of the veins that are outside the tongue is helped after the disorder of the cephalic, and it is by constricting the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and with diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sailor is such that the diseases are between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks out from each side one black vein: therefore heal both and do not move too much, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the ear that are commonly healed are healed in two ways: either by pinching at all the flame murderous, or by subtle cuts as if cutting through, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has the skill to open veins that are closed and flat with large blood visible, and that contain large blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the flame mirror.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtlely pointed, and is for purifying veins that are subtle, where there is subtle blood yellow.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The purification of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the shoulder, and where the belly; and it is necessary for the purifier to purify wisely, and to separate the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, it should be cooled, as I have said; and it should not be pricked with fire, but cut off as I have said.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the priest does not clearly open it, it is necessary to remove and replace it; or you want any rain of it, or you smear it in place of the vein on the arm: it opens clearly; and he cuts it off as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the vein of the sinew, it is necessary to remove and stretch the arm until you touch the vein; then sign the vein of the elbow, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with fire as we have said; and watch that you do not cut into the artery when you see the vein swell, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding high as a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, it is from an artery: hurry then, and place your hand longwise, then remove your hand without stopping, as many times as it happens; hold the arm still, and leave it thus, and do not move the hairs until it is healed; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it hurts you, and the medicine is not present, then cut open the artery if it opens, for the main part of the blood is drawn; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a small splinter of bread, and make it into a poultice, and take one half and place it on the other side; if it is not moistened, it is good; if not, then the cure, as we have said, with powders that moisten wounds; and the moistening is not greasy in many positions for the small wound of the limb, and the position of the bandage of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle is helped if it treats blood from above, and the body from below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the bandage to go through all the nerves that are out of place, and if it does not too much in front, and it finds the nerve, and it inflates and the salve is either greasy, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often opens, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtlety, then you must use the bandage from the instrument anesil; and protect the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein is helpful, as it draws blood from the head and helps with those; and it should be tapped by pricking the olive oil or mint leaf, for this is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries in it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is best to seek the lightest vein, and do not hurt anything if you cannot find it the first time, and then try again; and sometimes the veins swell in some people, but it does not matter the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about hygiene is that hygiene is only intended to maintain health and to ward off diseases to come; and it should be done in one of the three ways that are either cold or warm: namely, cephalic, federal, and basilic; and if one must practice hygiene at the beginning of the day, in the morning, and in the evening after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and if one must practice hygiene on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing salve that is administered to diseases has no fixed duration, but rather depends on the age and strength of the patient, in all hours and in all times; and it does not suit to heal children under the age of fourteen, nor a pregnant woman except for the first four months after the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one heal the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When one wishes to heal, in any way that may be, it is necessary for him to cleanse the intestines of a light clyster, if he has much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract the excessive and harmful superfluities to the main members; nor should one heal those who are too fond of meats, or drunkards, as much as they may be, or hydrocaphiacs; and if one wishes to heal after a colic passion, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent abdominal travels, pregnancy, watching, and fasting, and whatever the virtue, whether by an armor or a body; then subtly the humors, if it is not too thick, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have them; then take a bath or a shower, if nothing prevents, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the vein about the third hour, as we have said; and guard that day of work, and of pining, and of luxury, and of similar things; and be bound and joined, and let the healer be higher than those who heal, and let the friction of the arm twice or three times, then strain the joint gently, for when it is too strong or weak, it cannot correct the sin; and then friction the hand on the limb, as long as the veins swell, and feel that they are on; then wipe the healer with a little flame of old oil, then put his dose of his right hand above the vein of the limb wherever he wishes to heal, so that the vein does not fail to strike.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flee as if they were strings to the leeches, and if there are such ones that are plain of spaciousness, so that when one puts on the flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those; and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, because it is necessary that the leeches be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, then one should try again a little below that vein or higher, if the leeches are not inflated.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the joint is swollen, and the pain subsides within one or two days, and you do not bind the arm: perhaps it will become infected; do not enter water, then begin the healing if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, or without a cut, gently and subtly cut into it, and you doubt that there will be much blood as you saw, then firmly apply the flame directly to that wound; and the work is done roughly, provided the joint is swollen; for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the joint swelling, do not begin the healing again, and place a little oil on it, for it alleviates the flow of blood, and is useful in this joint as the oil; and thus administer the oil in every healing that you heal the wounds, to stop the flow of blood; and this also does three times and boils down, when placed on the joint; gently cut into it and spread it out when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there are large abscesses that often occur, even when not treated until this time or the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry and place a soft sponge soaked in boiling water and wrapped in a cloth on the limb for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the issue of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any length of time without turning black or green, you must not remove it; and if you see any sign of discoloration, place something like aloe or mercurous chloride mixed with honey or calamint on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often it appears as an abscess and the appearance of the base of the church: place your hand on it, and if you feel the bone pressing under your hand, that is the wrong appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything on it that we have said, because by chance you might cut the artery; but first apply a dry plaster to harden the bone, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And follow each vein according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is suitable for those who are weak and unable to bear the pain, and those who have the skill of arrow extraction, one should make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and let them rest often, and let the wound be cauterized by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of cauterization is safe from the breaking of bones and the tearing of nerves, and it is better than the cauterization done long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose body needs cauterization, it is suitable to give them bread moistened in the juice of green pomegranates; if they are hot-tempered, take out the arrow three or four times and apply the cauterization; and if they are of cold constitution, before the cauterization, give them bread moistened in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he palms the wound after much bleeding of blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of char, and sweet-smelling syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to strengthen an arm, and wound again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bandage gradually and gradually, according to the amount of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to wound again an arm after the first bleeding, and he has great pain, he should bandage seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the second hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal on the other side, they should heal according to the second hour or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For they have much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever; if one must draw out great quantities, and widen the vein until it gushes out; then one must apply all the conditions of healing, and place one's hand upon the pulse as it heals, that the patient does not return to the vein before healing, and this happens many times when the healer is negligent; and one should not press too hard when one sees the arm is ready to be released, and draw out blood the second time, and the vein is closed, but if it is curved, extend the arm gently, for that would be harmful; but let it remain as it heals the second time; or you should not go to the tip of the flame, until the blood frozen in the vein comes out, and put a little ointment on the wound, and press firmly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if it flees, let it go and do not hold it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, draw the blood from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is safer than the main one because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of drawing blood is that the hairs are heated in hot water until they turn red; then it is moved gently so that the vein appears well, then draw blood from the side, not too narrow or too long; and make the punctures wide, and draw blood well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be released, put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow out in the hot water until you have enough; and if it is still there, do not move the hand again, because it will put more in than before; and drawing blood from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the hand of the right side is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the way: strain the hand, and boil in hot water until the vein is outflowed, if one can see it; and if the salve is against the way, and if you cover it with all at once, it will not hurt anything; and do not move too much, because the nerves are all exposed to the fire, and then put the hand in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to sew quickly, and thus do for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The right side of the hand is useful for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The left side of the hand is useful for all diseases that are outside the body, such as diseases of the marsh, retention of urine, and diseases of the feet, knees, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its hand is that diseases are cured by putting hot and sharp things into it, and rubbing them on the vein until they rot, and tie above the joint; and the vein is at the elbow, and from there many rains come out; therefore, the hand with a large vein or at the elbow is more useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have healthy bones above the joint, and you are warned by the nerves that are dislocated, and the healthy part is crossed as in copulating; and let the flames be equal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the bone, reset the joint in high places, and let the vein well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first attempt is not successful, start the second attempt above a little, for the bones are salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make the other joint equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the neck is at the elbow, and its resetting is equal to the pain of the back, when it comes to arrow removal.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his health is such that the hairs between or in bathing, and is strange above the ankle four times in twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if she opens, then heal in all ways that you can, and transversely; and it is worth while to cover, for the less are salty, and it is very replete with hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not straighten it, then heal none of those that open or do not close at the small door, and turn to the little one, and guard against the nerves; and correct so much blood as you see, and then release the ligament, and put on cotton and keep it tight; she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction wounds are made of thorns, or of iron, or of glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways: either at all fire, or without fire; and suction done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve places on the body, of which one is completely on the chest; and the others are behind the neck; and the other two are on both sides of the neck; and the suction below the chin; and the suction on both shoulders; and the suction above the heels; and the suction on both arms; and the suction on both legs; and the suction on both ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, only small veins that are scattered in the body, and for this it does not weaken anyone, as is done with the treatment of a vein; and it should not be administered at all fire or without fire, in any disease due to repletion, until the whole body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	If necessary for diseases, it is recommended to ventose, or by customs, to anesthetize every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and every time; for there are some who, when they have the need to ventose, have heavy breathing; and some who feel repletion and heaviness in their face, and in their head, and at their neck; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have protruded their tongue, and reach for blood; and there are some who sing, and see through blood and mucous and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we order them to fast after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The fasting of the mind helps with the headache … that comes from the eyes, and it should only be done after the evacuation of all the blood; and this fasting is in the place of the fasting of the cephalic, and it should only be used by those who are of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, because this does great harm; and for this reason it should not be used by those who are awake or who have other cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often have this, become forgetful, and for that reason, it is necessary to place the vacuum a little more below due to the doubt of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The vacuum on the neck is in place of the sinus and the basilica, and for this reason, it is necessary to place it at the narrowest point, and to pierce the promontory of the channel, and to all, and to replenish; and it should be placed a little, because if it is held too tightly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The vacuum on the II costelz of the neck is necessary for headaches, and obtunding and emigration, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the sinus of the basilica; and it is necessary to command the saint to express his hand when placing it, that he does not compress the artery, and does not cause the evacuation of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilations of the neck are useful for diseases of the mouth, and decay of teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the remedies of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the shoulders are useful for diseases that come from heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations of the elbows are as useful as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and commands the healer not to pierce too deeply, for the skin is bare of flesh, and knows of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The vacuum that is on the back should be used to remove swellings from the base, and for diseases of the spine, and it should be a large, metal one, that can draw well; and by chance, if it is too thin, it might break; and I cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The vacuums of the legs heal openly, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the joints, and of the bones, and of the bladder, and remove swellings; and they are in the knees, and in the ankles, and everywhere they weaken the body after long use, and bring on fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the vacuum is that you first apply it empty and quickly succeed, then press it firmly and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the liver red and swollen, and appear the flow of blood; then stop, and replace the vacuums, and take care in the position of the body, for there are such people who have tender flesh and clear skin: it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make wide wounds and a deep one; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to finely puncture the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very sharp, then you must strike it a third time; and when we wish to draw out the arrow little by little, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out much blood, we should often recommend it; and if the bone is not sharp, then strike it in front, and the end should be perceived firmly, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are rough, that you rub the legs of the suction cups with an appetizing and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, with pennyroyal, lavender, camomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of tamarisk, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person who is to be treated with a hot bath and wide pores, then one should not put any oil, but it should be washed after the vaporization of high rose water, or high cold water, or marjoram water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash, or high mint water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive swellings rise from old wine, or from sour wine, or from the decoction of anise or chamomile, or from other similar things; and they should not immediately be purged after the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep immediately after ventosation, and it is good that they sweat, when they should be ventosed and when they are being ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are being purged are feverish, and if they are not too weak and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as large green apples and endives and leeks at the sauce, and similar things; and they should drink watered mustard, and cinnamon and cloves, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold constitution should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine between old and new, and a little mustard, and small pinch of peppercorns and pigeons; and the day that they are about to vomit, they should drink more than they eat; and it is appropriate to give some men three or muscat grapes before or after vomiting, to strengthen the main members; and the subtle ones should not drink, but only those who are strong.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed on the body to relieve pain are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and podagra, and on the belly and the buttocks, and the thighs, because these members do not suffer much from being touched, and no one does this except to draw blood from one member to another, as we place suction cups on the breasts when the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the belly and on the buttocks to soothe the member; and remove pain, when there is an abscess or a stone, if by its attractive power it removes the abscess, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it is done when placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for sweat alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes with hot water, as in diseases of the chest, and in such a way that one fills the suction cup with hot boiling water, or hot water where there are harmful herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two wide and half-palm-sized openings and a small puncture in the middle, as to put a needle, and it should be of tin, or sulfur before it does not burn the hairs when placing it on the limb; and it should have in the middle a thin rod of tin or iron, to place a candle, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the vacuums of children are different from those of adults, and of the weak from the strong.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or iron rod, and put it through the suction cup's tube, so that it clarifies at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the hairs; then put it on the limb, and you should do so on the part that we have mentioned, so that when one wants to, if there is vapor, and remove the suction cup; and take the iron rod as before, and repeat often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is used in the disease of pleurisy, there is no tube or nipple, and it is not administered until it is full of vapor, and it is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not suitable for treatment except in members where it is impossible to place suction due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar members, such as teeth and nostrils, and others like them; and the quality of the user is that when you remove sansues that are in shallow waters without pressure, take; and put them in shallow water, as long as they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse with blood and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put the sansues on; and when they are flat and blackened, if it is a place where suction can be placed, place it, for this is very helpful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, first raise the limb from the wrist, and then from the elbow, very well, and then wipe it; and if the wound is too large after the course of the sinews, then dip a cloth in cold linseed oil, and place it on top, until the sinews are cleansed; and if the sinews multiply, then place vitriol or salts on top, and similar things, until they are cleansed; or you place half-peeled beans on the wound, and leave them until they stick to the limb, and now it will stop bleeding; and if you have more serious wounds, take other bandages.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the snakes refuse to take, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you place a needle until the snake bites, and then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will die; and when you see that they are dying, powder with a little aloe and ground silk, or ashes, so they will now be gone.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Be aware, dear son, that the foolish people of this chapter have never seen any of the old books, nor have they read any letters; and for this reason the science is hidden in our land, because I found none good; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise put his understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced seek and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or wound comes to any part, it is necessary to treat the injury on one side and the other, if nothing happens, such as weakness of the body, or children, or the elderly; or if the wound is not very clean, or too cold; and to use hot cholz, that is to say, hot jute and kidney, and do not drink wine, and do not change any fatty charcuterie, and do not fill oneself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of an abscess, or spread of matter in the member; if the injury returns to its previous government as it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a thick mash of meat that causes swelling, such as cooked wheat, and risotto, and tests, and fish, and chicken, and eggs, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the mash should be applied frequently and soon after the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the elderly and infirm do not heal well or mend according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset and join the bone together with large strong ones that hold and support the member together, until it is enforced so much as it was before; and not entirely of its own work, and for this reason it is necessary to apply a thick mash of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and I will tell you all the ways of fracture in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes through the spine, and another in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own method and proper tool in restoration, according to what memory comes in the limb; and fracture of bone is known by the bone being twisted, and open widely by itself, and pressing against the palm; and when there is no crookedness or touching, and the pains are not great, if there is no fracture; but it can still have crookedness, or cut, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it by hand, but place the remedies that come here after, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the broken part that was in the arm, and the two parts are disjointed, you must now put them evenly, as long as pus comes out; and if pus thickens and comes, do not let any scar remain until the pus is calmed; then set it lightly and carefully, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that where there are pieces, then restrain it as it should be hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	If the bone is broken into pieces, if it is a hand or foot, or if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member broken are separated, you should gently move each addition in its place as you can, and guard that by your work not come the bad injury or pain; and well join the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it cleans beautifully, and do not strain it too much, and do not press as those who bring by their work abscess and contraction to the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a point, well chastise the pain so it does not move, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way; and keep it securely so that the limb feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is almost at a point, and it should be put in the right position so that it feels no pain; and guard that it is put correctly, so that twisting does not come when it is returned; and the quality of the limb broken is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The quality of the limb broken is different in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if they are thin, cover them with thin linen cloths; and those that are thick, such as thighs and calves: if they are thick, wrap them in a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bands embrace the whole member evenly, and hold it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap lightly around three or four times according to the size of the member, and hold your hand a little on each bandage, then go above the break and hold it less than the break; then soften the bandage a little and little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage and return immediately above the broken part; then return to the part away from the break and hold it evenly, neither too hard nor too strongly, as we have said in the first paragraph above; then place between the bandages linen or cloth, as much as they are equal, then tie everything above a bend, and then put your well-made fingers on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
