Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or boil, put something soothing on it to draw out the pus, and what removes the abscess, and leave it like that for some time; then apply compresses on it, and be made of a piece of cloth cut evenly, or of a stick used to make clips, or of palm leaves, and be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the compress that one puts on the wound should be slightly larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as the limb is small or large; then apply compresses as you did in the first layer, then tie them up with a thread evenly, as you did in the first layer over the wound; the tighter they are, the less; and it should be that the threads are medium, not too thick or too thin, and be made of linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of those who make their bandages from twisted linen ropes, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should only have about two fingers' space between each compress.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the thorns after the straining in their place, put discharge from them with linen, or other clean cloth, so that it does not fester.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the stitches are broken, I will tell you the treatment here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put splints on them until after five or seven days, or more depending on your safety from abscess; and see the method of the ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and you should take flour that is kept in the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of egg, and use this mixture, not too thin or too thick, and it is the common method of the plaster restoring fracture at many positions, and especially to women and small children, because it is not too hard or too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to apply plasters for fractures and dislocations and twists: take alabaster and ladanum and enulae and asefetida and Arabic gum and mugwort, an ounce each; wormwood and aloes, an ounce each; alechil eight ounces; and make a powder, and mix it with honey; if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it will quickly heal broken bones, and it is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to apply plasters for twists: take mugwort and valerian, an ounce each; wormwood and aloes, fourteen ounces; acaice six ounces; bolic armenic ten ounces, and grind it well, and mix it with vinegar or honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method to treat joints and bones that are dislocated from their sockets, and to relieve the pain, and to use the tail of the bone, and the fracture: take a new bone, and moisten it in oil and cooked fat, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal immediately, but it is good for relieving abscesses and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method to treat broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthworms, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method to treat the break in the bone and to ease the remaining pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of wormwood, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one in parts; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are cold, mix with moist or dry coriander seed, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of treatment, more suitable than the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of wormwood, linseed, balm, mint, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; grind, and mix with salt, or moist or dry coriander seed, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb except for a plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to heal, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to bandage that is good for wounds and pain: take hair from the tail of a horse or feathers of an owl, and viscous substance and silk, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a bandage and put it on the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then release it a little later, and be careful if the pain does not disappear, or if the bone of its joint does not move; then do not release it by force again. If the pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or inflammation, quickly release it, and remove the poultice now; and take light linen, and moist sea sponge, and plunge in hot water, and lift the limb until the itching ceases, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened with hot oil or rose oil, and tie with a nut, as long as you are sure of no abscess forming; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and soothe the pain, then begin the subtle bandage again, and a little poultice, and do not strain it as much as before; subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and inflamed, and you have knowledge of plasters and ointments, then apply them evenly as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb within three or four or five or seven days, and you leave it for twenty days, as we see, until the breaker is aware, and approaches the joint above; then restrain it more than before, and increase its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the limb is dryer than necessary, scrape it with sharp hot tongs every time you apply it, and this every hour, and loosen the bandage a little; by this method then the necrosis is stopped in the limb, and it is healed quickly, unlike what the foolish people do, who cause great pain to the limb: this is bad, and if it is done improperly, I see nothing else but weakness and working incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of breaking, and various figures, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collar bone completely breaks the bone just below it which is outside the bone, as if it were cut or broken; and for this reason this kind of break is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above in a piercing manner, and this kind of break is called «absolute»; and it is the wound of these two breaks, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion from a fall, or a cut from a sword, or a break from a fall on stone, or from falling onto something else, and similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a broken bone that pierces through the skin, approaching the flesh on either side of the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is set into the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called "capillary" fracture; and if the wound made by being struck by an arrow, or falling, or something similar, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and the threads are like those of a hat when they are sewn together; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens more often in those who have or are mostly moist bones, such as children; and they have all these ways of fracture that small pieces are displaced like these; and I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fractures by the displacement above them, and the inspection of tents, and by the rotten char that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known because when one has revealed the bone, and one rubs it above, if there is an open black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, be careful about the bad accident, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and turning red, and other similar things in many dispositions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any apparent injury, and you hope for recovery, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day or you will not be able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the arm, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the flesh around the bone has not decayed, and the injury that we have mentioned occurs.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the broken piece of bone comes close to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary to cut away the part that is wounded in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound more smoothly than you can, and when blood comes out when revealing the bone, or an abscess forms, help with what is necessary, and it is necessary to fill the wound with linen cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed down, and be sure that no blood comes out; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two methods of craft: one method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then use another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several cuts of different sizes, some narrow and some wide, and they are sharp and made of iron, and work lightly, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and outside, it is necessary that you pierce around it, as long as you administer cuts with drills, not before it goes through the test, and it should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each one comes in its own place of the edge of the bone, so that you have drills for all teeth; and this is the form of the three methods of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To perform a fire cauterization through the bone, you should place the iron on the bone, and turn it back to your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the iron on another part slightly later, and so do all around, then cover the incisions the space of the bone between the teeth, and do it as subtly as you can, and clearly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is advisable to close the opening that remains in the bone with another instrument similar to an incision, but it should be more tenacious and more subtle than the other incision; and if there remain any small bones or scales, remove them gently with the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is such that the Galians call it, which is much better; and they say it is very good.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have removed that part, then place the lens-shaped piece of this incision, which is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and it is the piece of that side, so that the cutter is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is against the bone, then lightly cut the bone, because one cuts it well without harming, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only broken on one side, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the scales with a thin razor that you should have in various quantities, to manage each limb as conveniently as possible, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have large razors before, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair clippers and subtle fractures, you should manage it according to its progression; and this is a thing that is not repeated by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a strip of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another strip doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first strip; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer by pouring over an additional layer of linen, and do not strain it until it stains the wound only; leave it in this way for one or two days, until the abscess is relieved, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lis roots, flour of vegetables, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer additional medicines without biting; and keep the wound clean, so that you do not leave any tissue or pus, because when pus accumulates on the skin, it causes the skin to rot and it hurts greatly.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take precautions therefore, as no accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other remedy comes to the patient, which has virtue, it is necessary that you apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and a cloth, and put it on the wound; then cure with methods of cures as it is appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Be careful that the two bones of the shoulder are not broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is twisted or dislocated, and then it is healed.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you break your small nail or needle at the tip of your finger, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the bone regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and keep in mind that the pain should not be felt through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone, and cannot reach your finger, it is necessary that you place it at the top of a small stick or a slightly thick one.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, make another one, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then place at the top of your finger tents of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you are on the other side, where the fracture is; and the tents should be so large that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no one should mash the tents in the fire, and each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be mashed in the making of an ointment with honey and powder of mollusk; then leave the tent until the bone is hard, and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never use feathers in place of tents, and if you have a soft cloth around, and hold the fracture, and blow the pains through it; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you work, put clay or a cotton ball soaked in red wine or a little hydrogen peroxide on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If abscesses do not come to the nose, put a poultice of wheat flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk on it, then put light cloths over it and do not tie the nose tight; if the broken piece of the nose is small and broken into smaller pieces, remove them with suitable instruments, then cut the wound, and treat other injuries as appropriate, and bandage it with appropriate emplastrums and ointments, and if there is no wound in the nose, treat it with tents and put cold compresses on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is only slight, and not completely broken into two pieces, as can be seen if one looks carefully.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, to push your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left side, to push your index finger from the right hand, and gently push the fracture inwards, and hold it with the other hand by default, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is in two pieces, it is necessary that you administer traction of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth avails, or breaking, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place it over the broken jaw, and place it over one double cloth; and place over the cloth a great well-made bandage, or a piece of leather even and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the muscle that you can, and command the patient not to move, and feed them with light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, remove it from the patient and then put it back in place; and apply a poultice on top, of flour from the mill with plenty of urine or semolina flour, after having removed the crust; and apply the poultice again lightly, and if the poultice sticks, leave it until it is healed; often healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, bandage carefully with any piece of the bone that is broken off; so gently as to avoid further damage.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, if the wound is wide, then apply wound dressings to it, to drain pus until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forearm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forearm is broken several times in front and behind the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated into two pieces, and there are fragments, and it is the least heavy to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And when the fracture is in the presence of a wound, you should have two ministers, one to apply the splint that covers the broken bone; and the other to extend the neck towards the affected part; then set the fracture equally on both sides, so that it forms as it should, without any appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a rounded ball of cloth or linen, and as large as your need; extend and support the broken bone, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you set the fracture equally.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder of the arm out, because it comes from above, then it is necessary that the hairs be pulled evenly over its surface, and move the shoulder outwards, and bend the minister's elbow down, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the fracture to your two hands, and if you find the broken pieces, it is necessary that you make them join; and gently pick up the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but put the instrument away from the arm, to guard against infection:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems like a spoon, and is not tightly closed, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and it has two prongs, if you see, and one is wide and the other narrow, like the edge of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of an abscess, if the wound is large, or you doubt an abscess, then use the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if it is soft, then soak the cloth in rose oil and in vinegar and in wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The application of the bone, when it is in pain and in position, is that you place the plaster of the mill powder and an additional doughnut on the bone, and put light bandages on, and place a sphere outside the joint, if you have the skill; then take a very large bandage of one palm wide, then double the cloth over the bandage and the plaster; then take a thin staff of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the large bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging down; and place the staff on the breaker, and turn the bandage over the neck, and outside the joint, and outside the bad joint; and bandage each part, and when you see that the limb holds the breaker evenly, and you see clearly that the staff does not move over the broken bone, reward every day, and when the joint is released, restrain it; and place the bad side on his back, and put a small bandage outside the joint, to raise the dislocation in the shoulder; if it aligns the force of the arm by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not release it unless something bad happens, for up to 20 days; then restart the plaster, if you see that there is a need, and bind and leave it as long as it is restored; and it is restored in the most 28 days, and less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or is out of its place, and it only heals by touch; then according to the figure of the fracture, and the bone is placed back in its natural form, in all ways you can; then put powder from the mill with abundant oil on the bone, and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it; then put a wide but thin board, a bit wider than the shoulder, and if the board touches any part of the shoulder, use a strip of linen to make the board even; and then tightly wrap it around everything with a strong bandage, so that the board does not move from its place, and watch the joint every day; and every time it breaks, tighten and put the board back in its place if it is off, and ease the pains on its side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 30 days, And when these numbers are completed, remove and be careful, for this is not bone that heals quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is torn off before the wound is opened, and not removed from the surrounding area, then cut through it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the splint to alleviate an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the splint
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in the middle, but this rarely happens; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines towards the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of movement, and everything, and possibly vomits blood, and the wound opens in the broken bone, and the smell is bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the hairs lie silently above their backs, and the metal between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and gather the ribs of the two ribcages in your hands, and subtly put them evenly in all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put on plasters and poultices above the spine with salt or other light material, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so it does not move; and turn the limb gently to the back, and gradually tighten, and every hour massage the limb, and if it moves, tighten; and if it is necessary to release, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and release it, and clean the plaster, and address what has come from methods of treatment; then reset the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fractures of the ribs come only from great blows on the back and at the top, and they do not break unless because they are sharp; and the pain is felt well during the examination of them.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and the bandage of a splint if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inclined inward, it causes great pain and tenderness, as if from a pleurisy, because the ribs do not touch the skin; and they must be pressed, and everything else, and there is much bleeding of blood, and this is a difficult sickness, and the ancients have taken great care.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if among those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, to push the broken bone into place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, if pus does not come, unless it comes.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then cleanse it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that among those who put suction cups on the limb, for draining well, and this is reasonable; nevertheless, doubt and there is where the suction cup does not attract the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that among those who must cover the limb with linen oiled high, and one puts tents between the ribs to keep the lung evenly inside, then treat the care of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain is great that he cannot bear it through the bone that does not touch the skin, and there is doubt, then you must cut across the broken ribs on the side, and you must place an instrument to protect the wound; and then you must saw the bone, and gently pull, and then stitch the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the skin, then place moistened cloths on it in rose oil, and put on the affected area; and treat while the skin of what is needed for the abscess, and lie quietly nearby until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck bone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when a breaker breaks the neck bones, and there is hardly any pain; and similarly at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them and do not, it means that the bone joint is saved, and the pain has been cured, if you put care on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine in the back, and you see if it is healthy or not, if it holds still with soft feet, and if the accidents that are in hand are those that are on the back, and above the back there is ventosity and involuntary excretion; and when it is placed on its belly, if there is involuntary excretion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is placed on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is deadly: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the care is such that you reward if there is an abscess clean, put on the spine oil of rose or goose fat, as long as it is calmed; then put on one of the healing plasters and drying, and bind with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where you feel the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dry, it is necessary to cover it with the cure; then remove the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if it is large, at a seam, then treat the wound with an ointment rubbing charcoal, as long as it is healed; and if the patient's bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow", if you have a bottle of your right hand, and put it even on the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the bandage over, if you have the skill; then tighten, and if there is dry bone, do it again, and remove, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are fractured, and if it does happen, it is not much different from a slight dislocation; making it long, and declining to the side, and coming to the shoulder, causing great pain, swelling, and inflammation where the bone is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the fractured part; and remove any fragments of the broken bone, and restore its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then keep it in place until it is restored to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long or it inclines towards the inside, place the injured limb on its belly until the healing of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have placed it in position, apply the poultice, then place it on a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fracture so it does not move; and bandage the limb along the sides, until the fracture is straightened.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on their uninjured side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess forms and comes out, do not touch it until the abscess is soothed, and follow the method we have previously mentioned; then return to the healing process, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad event; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoire is what is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a smooth bone, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two bones together, and raise them up, and saw the misaligned part above the seat; then pour some brine on the broken bone, as much as it can bear, and put a hook of wood on it, then place something heavy or the assistant extends it downwards; then put the broken pieces together with their hands together, until the broken one returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to place the dislocation above its shoulder, and hold the hand on its collar, then command two ministers that one ties what is above the breaker at his hands, and the other ties behind everything, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the rope outside the breaker, above the breaker, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breaker is close to the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place the rope outside the armpit, and the other towards the back, outside the breaker; and similarly, if the breaker is towards the back, it is necessary to place the rope gently, without labor, until the breaker is even above the shoulder, and above the back; then equalize the breakage, as it should be, and stretch it, if there are no signs of apostematous chaus.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess arises and comes, if it is not restrained for seven days, and put in a poultice of mold and rose oil, until the abscess is soothed; then restrain, and the manner of restraining is that you place the plaster on the broken part, then bring the arm up with the assistance, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and bandage, and restrain with the assistance, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, and have two inches of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on each side; then strain against the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter over the fracture, more strongly and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the position of the splints and the strain, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is healed, let it lie for seven days, as we have said; then look at the joint every three days, that it does not prick or swell, or that the scarring does not come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the dislocation, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur within three hours or more, and the pain remains on his back, and his hands are on his stomach; and he puts a piece of linen cloth evenly across the injury, and looks every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the member does not move, or that the tendons are not softened; then the dislocation will be cured by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have already mentioned, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle; and when he begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the dislocation and the leg should be reset in 40 hours after everything; and then one should apply and administer warm water and medicines of ointments to the limb to promote healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If its structure is crooked and swollen, it may take 1 or 2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "forearm," which are small, and it is this one that forms the cavity; and the other is large, and it is this one that is outside, towards the little one; perhaps the large forearm breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the healing is light, and the cure; and when large bones are broken, the healing is difficult, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is necessary to extend them slightly and align them evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it is necessary to pull them more forcefully; and extend them over the cushion, and tie the hand at a higher level than the other fingers, and the small fingers lower than the others, and so that the joints cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of them higher, so that the joints do not suffer any labor; then extend the assistants to the part away from their hand, or to the elbow, and other assistants above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no piece that can be held, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken piece there is a wound, I have spoken of it to the chapter's master; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there is an abscess, then use the poultice made of rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and tie the poultice gently, until the abscess is relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the crust, and apply the powder from the mill with plenty of urine, then place the splints, and set the splint of the broken bone closer than the others, and a bit wider than the others; and make sure it has six splints or more: whether the broken bone is in one of the bones, or in two; and hold it higher than the broken bone than any other part, and always less in removing, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are above the broken bone be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, which is used to tie it, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	If any misfortune comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must raise the limb in hot water for as long as those itches are soothed; and let the limb rest without being too tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the strapping, and if the joint is dislocated and the bones are broken, or similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and let it rest for some time, until the swelling has passed, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to harm, then let it wait for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if it is within the body, then put your hands on its neck, and make its neck even, and guard against movement and digestion, and sleep on its back; and after 30 or 35 days, or perhaps 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	After the back of the hand and to us there are few breaks, and it only happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plantar surface of the hand is broken or injured, it is necessary that the painful parts be straightened and aligned correctly; then put your hand on the extended palm, and extend the healer's broken bones, and place them evenly with the other, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no wounds, then put a splint according to the size of the limb; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the bone is broken in the peroneal region of the plantar arch, make a bandage of cloth, and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken foot; then stretch it into a long strip, and let it be as wide as the plantar arch of the hand, and stretch it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the bone is broken in the posterior region, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below in the foot, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and stabilize the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the broken bone comes to any of the two digits, whether it is the pinky or another, it should be aligned as needed; then wrap it with the plantar arch, and if you see that you need to place a straight small splint to lift the broken bone and not move it; and if the broken bone is in other fingers, such as the index or another, align it as needed, and the joint with the healthy finger next to it; or you can hold them all together, which is better, or you can place a splint above, as appropriate; and take care of restoration and joint positioning, and treat what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the rib are often broken, and one can see it when they return in front and behind; and its restoration is that one puts the bone above the broken part, and the other outside.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the hairs are cut off from its face, then each assistant stretches his part equally; and this is when the break is put in place of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the rib, then one of the ribs towards the base, and the other ribs outside the broken part.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the kidneys, and then one of the ribs above the kidneys, and the other ribs below the broken part. Then put the mirror the bone equal to its two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and the bandage, unless there comes a swelling.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that has opened, let it calm down then return to your work and your treatment; the matter is done in a similar manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the broken bone with a double or triple layer of cloth, and let the excess remain; then bend the leg until the heel reaches the base of the knee, and tie a long piece of cloth between the thigh and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the upper end of the cloth to the top; then bend the cloth over the leg and the thigh, and place the bandage on the broken bone; then put a bandage on the leg bone; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to equalize the tension, then begin to bind it in three or four layers above the broken bone; and as you go higher than the broken bone, and less tightly; then examine the two pieces of cloth that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and the three bandages that are above, then return to the top of the cloth, until you reach below the knee joint; and if it does not move from its place, then let it remain thus, so that there is no abscess or swelling of any kind.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it is dislocated, then release it, and put it back as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that can be felt, then it should be set, if possible; and if not, then it must be broken, and pulled straight; and the cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never break the ribs in this way, as in the dislocation and shoulder; however, in the restoration made thus does not hurt the bones.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is important that the ribs are restored at different times, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the road of the gentleman
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that on the road of the gentleman there is little breakage, but it rains many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a puncture, and it has to all wounds, and without wound, and this feels very bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts what is broken back together as much as possible; then put the plaster, and if you have the skill, put a round bandage, and hold it as it should be, then reward all the preparations that we have said in other broken things, such as abscess and similar; then put to each accident what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right, and the other is called "foscile"; and all the other fractures are as they come to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the equal arm, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg returns to all its parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then it returns in front.
