Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and it returns outside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply gentle traction, and make it even, and tie the fractures equally; however, if there is a break and it is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the traction should be less and lighter; and the alignment according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that bind the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough to go from the knee to the ankle; then wrap them around and tie them in the middle, and at this point it will not allow the leg to bend to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one administers the long strips of cloth, and if it is made properly, and correctly place the leg in a splint to prevent movement, and properly do this in the fracture where he has the wound; and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; until the cure is as healthy as possible.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones due to piers
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no breaking of bones, but in the case of piers, there is never breaking of bones and it is not necessary, and only a slight injury occurs in some cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breaking of bones due to piers, and you see these bones sticking out over each other, then put the foot on the ground, as if it wants to walk, and then place your foot where the bones are raised, then press them so much that they return to their place; then apply the ointment and bandage above, and put a small piece of cloth on the wound of the foot, then strap it to the foot evenly, then wrap dressings around, and other things that you have at hand.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone is released, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you reset them as we have said for the two bones of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and make it slightly wider, then place the bandage as I have said, and strain evenly; and if there are two or three or more broken, place a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strain the bandage away from the skin of the bone; and let it be above the head of the bone below the belly of the bone, so that it heals well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are fractured, if the wound is enlarged, then incline it to the part of the back, and hold it from behind; then fill the wound with nature's cotton, and put in as much as possible; then lift the woman, and gradually raise her back, and when the cotton comes out of the wound, return the bone with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, return it, and thus do this for seven days or so: then the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of berries, and tie a cat to it, and blow all the berries into the wound; then blow into the cat in a form, until the bladder is empty inside: nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these fractures are not hidden to those who put their study and practice into it, and pay attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in many positions the right way of restoration: understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the bone, when it is broken, take a goose quill and blow into the bone; then wrap it in cloths, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleansed immediately, so that the cleansings that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if the dressing of vinegar, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fractured bone in the same hour, or the next day, if there are no pus.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes, then leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the pus is abated, and do not touch it on the following day or quarter, for you would bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken teeth appear above the gum line, it is necessary that you gently place them in your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not equipped to be placed evenly in your hands, use an iron tool with seven or eight inches of length, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this reason, it should have three or four prongs, according to how many it has in each treatment of broken bones; and it should be round and a bit thick, so that it does not pierce through the limb at your work, and it should be sharp behind, and wide in the middle in front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient must have the broken bone placed above the head of the visible bone; and the splint is applied once, as long as it returns, and it should be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the splints cannot well hold the bone, then it is necessary to cut the head of the bone until the splints have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then use a suitable tool for this purpose, such as a saw or a file, to your liking; then roughen and make small scratches on the bone that remains.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned to its place, and the pain is great afterwards, wait until it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do this until it is in its natural place, then moisten the bandage with black stiptic wine, and properly if it has been open; and do not put anything else on the wound where there is oil, that it does not cause pus and corruption to come; then administer these things as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take care that the wound is not stretched with the break; and many times this has been done by fools, and they have caused pus or death or corruption at any time; and let the strain be softer and gentler than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no evil accident has occurred, as we have said, and you relieve the pain to the limb, if it does not require to be put on splints; but wrap around, in place of splints, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two hours that the wound is bleeding again, remove what you have put on top of all the blood, and apply healing ointment, such as Tetrapharmacum and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you move the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the bow can move lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to protrude, and it cannot be healed but remains bent, saw off the small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you sew the wound with a tent, and remove all those unnecessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or in any other way of corruption, then it is necessary that you heal it, according to what it says in its chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open above the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not remove it, for many times death comes, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will fall out after 20 or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of blows that come from the welding
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the broken bone, exactly at the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the misalignment of the limb; and perhaps it cannot do its natural workings.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then if it is fresh, then administer stanching medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acaice, and similar things, either one or all together, and mix them with stiffening wine or with abundant honey or with garlic; and place it on the wound in a cloth, and keep it tightly, and do not let it leak out later; then remove it, and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you can place a piece of plaster well made; because the property of the plaster is that it removes all the inflammation from the limbs; and if the swelling has already hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the coping above, and making the superfluity apparent; or you can cut it with any knife until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains after the limbs are weak and subtle, there are many causes for this: one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not come to the proper position of the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer a bath, and give joy and ease; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great swelling, and the swelling often of hot water, until the swelling goes to the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after healing, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, it does not matter if its natural appearance is lost: thus do not believe those who say that one must break the limb completely new, and many have done this in our land; and such practices are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; however, if the dislocations and twisting are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot water or softening herbs that are cooked, such as willow leaves, roots, and mellilot, and similar things; and make a mollifying poultice, such as good-quality honey, and take willow bark powder, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the poultice on top; or take figs, and grind them with linseed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is it necessary to apply continuous and prolonged pressure with wet hands on the dislocation.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is awake and hard, like a stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, if it covers just above the bone, make a slight incision; and put on a bandage and care for the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be returned against the grain.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, the shoulder swells, and if by chance it is reset to the bone where it is swollen, because it does not matter that it moves at the angle where it is swollen: many times it brings on spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, first soothe the injury, then leave it until the abscess is calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the cure comes in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare that the mandibles are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both mandibles occur in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are entirely dislocated, hanging down towards the chin, and covering the lips so that he cannot hold them open, nor can he close his mouth, and it wraps around his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if she is whole and completed, it is necessary that you reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the minister sterilizes the head of the dislocation, and puts the mirror into the pocket of one of her hands at the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand be outside, to hold even; and command the dislocation to soften, its jaws, and move from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror moves evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if both jaws are involved, then raise the arms in hot water and oil, until they are lightly reset; do not delay the resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned evenly, and the mouth of the painful tooth is well closed to soften, put a cloth moistened with a warm, hardened wax made from rosin and wax, then lightly bind it with the molten wax; let the painful teeth sleep on their backs, and their jaws being between two cushions, so that they do not move to the left or right, nor strive to chew, but take light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are healed; then change what they want lightly, and do not work much to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour, and they are not converted back to their original shape, then fevers and sweats become common, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is a sign of danger; and often those who have it die within fourteen days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be removed from the side without causing further damage, and it is not reset once dislocated, and one can feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient should lie on their back, and extend their arms; then press the affected part firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the patient who is on the side cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated once, then reset it as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the patient with the dislocated shoulder is restored when it is healed from its injury.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: one is that it dislocates at the part of the socket below; and the second is at the part of the elbow above; and sometimes dislocates at the part above, and this happens little; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocates downwards towards the socket, especially to those who have little char, because to these it is difficult; to those who have enough char, it dislocates and returns quickly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some people, a fracture or crushing, and the shoulder swells with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is below the shoulder, and it sets apart the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them obvious differences; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the shoulder, the top of the shoulder, like as if it were two bones; and the bad hand cannot reach its neck, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will see it clearly below; and this kind of dislocation is only to be reset, when it is new, or if there are pains in the joint.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the hand of the injured person high, then places his fingers on the joint, and pulls the joint upward to the shoulder; and the minister lifts his hand, and extends it upward, putting it away; then it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said earlier, then it is necessary that the injured part be soaked in hot water; and the minister should warm and soften and moisten it with a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and then soak the injured part on its back, and place a piece of cloth evenly, neither too soft nor too hard, under the joint, then place the foot of the injured person on the cloth, and lift the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the injured person; and other ministers wet the head of the injured person, so that it does not move down; this shoulder is now all right, and you should see if the resetting is done as follows: and it is that you make sure that the person who is stronger than the injured part is directly opposite the costeit, and pull the shoulder away from the joint of the injured part, and lift the joint upward, so that the injured part hangs in the air; and other ministers take the hand of the injured person down towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, then with it nothing heavy can be done, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting is done in another way: and it is like this that one puts a long thin rope on the ground, where the injured can be held as if with a spear, but not too thick or too rough; then it is put away from the pain, but with cloth underneath, and the pain is kept at the long end of the staff; then his hand is stretched out on the other side, forming a shape, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if he does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a rope of two arms of great and four fingers wide, which has the head round to enter through the opening outside the shoulder, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie a soft cloth over the head where the dislocation is, which does not cause pain, then remove it from the dislocated area; extend one arm over the long one, and tie the helper over the dislocated area, and the other arm at the top of the shovel, then place your hand on the broad side of the shovel, and let your hands hang down, and let the body hang down on the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is healed in any way, it is necessary to place a bandage of equal linen over the shoulder, then apply the poultice with powder from the mill, with incense and a little oil, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove the bandage from the shoulder evenly, and return the limb to the poultice, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let your hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move it little, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then move it again after five or seven days, and if it is stiff and cannot be moved, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is very strong due to moisture that has come, or for other reasons, it is necessary that you administer cauteries at three points, as it is placed before or in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot raise the arm above, then cut the nerve at the top of the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and cut that the joint has never been fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is by the wrist and the fingers, or behind, is caused by impact and stretching of the hands, and there is another remedy; and treat until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb swells and moves poorly, then apply the hairs many times, until that swelling is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the shoulder joint is dislocated at points, and repeatedly dislocates; and it is dislocated from all parts, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation has not been remedied, as one can see and feel well; and it moves according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the misaligned ear with the healthy one, see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is cut, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as possible when the shoulder comes, for if the shoulder comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is in the back; it is better than other dislocations, but causes more great pain, and perhaps death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is so that one can reset, that you extend your hand to their two hands; and their arms are spread, and their hands on either side of the ear, inside and outside, and push the joint back together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and holds the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to the place, give strong extension; and if two people extend the arm, and hold it with two people, so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm from each part, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint at the hand, if you have any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, as much as it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster with some honey on top, and hold it firmly, and put the arm against the back of the bad shoulder, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, release the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, restart the bandage and the ligament, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly placed; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the movement of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is soothed; or put a piece of fat mutton grease on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and put in a bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint immediately, then put the grease back on, and put him in the bath again; and do this twice or three times until it is healthy; and if you see, then put some wet moistened with hot butter on, and strain it on; and it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. In any case, it should be quickly returned to its place in the same way as it was dislocated, whether the veins are swollen or there is an abscess present.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is done by placing the hand wrongly on a table, and extending the fingers of the hand, and the mirror shows that the palm should be placed over the appearance of the joint, and the arm should be moved until it is back in place; then you should check if it is properly set; afterwards, place the hand wrongly on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand on a table, and the other person places their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well. If not, apply the ointment of healing remedies and let it rest for a while before starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not put anything into the wound until the hand is clean, and nothing can be inserted at all: therefore cut the tendon or the artery; if there is no other method except to burn with a cauterizer over the case, and perhaps nothing else is suitable.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the poultice that we have said above, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved well, and there is no swelling, then boil water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of both hands
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never dislocate both hands at once, never at the back of the palm or the belly; then hold the hand, and reset the dislocation to your pouch as it returns, then support the chief of the hand, and push it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for three days, and then put it in place that day; and tie it, as we have said, and remove the bandage every day, and move it, and re-tie it; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine in the back or neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions jump out without volition, and cannot be held, and often the limbs are softened, or the two thighs or both arms or one; and often the spine moves at the back; this is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you reward the gilbositez if it comes from childhood; if there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or from impacts or from similar things, they said in the old ways of healing by great words, or it does not have much benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of the palsy which comes from the left side, there is no engineering or health; and also the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure it other than that proper one which comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the limbs should be stretched out over its face in the first place, and have some strain away from him, so that he does not blister; then make one bandage at the head on the ground, and the other at the feet, and tie a bandage outside the tendons of the limb, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and the assistant should fasten the bandages, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bandages; and they should be well tied, the bandage as we have said, and the hand puts its palms on the spine properly, until it regains.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If it does not return with this treatment, take a table of three arms' length, and twist it away from the body, and place the painful side against the table, then place the middle of the table on the spine; and put the patient's feet on the other end of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the twisted one that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should fasten two ropes to the head of the painful arm of a person, and on the other side of the feet, and between each rope, outside and inside, one span of length; and in each rope, one button, or where the twisted one corrects, and let the ropes be firmly on the ground, so that they do not move; and between each two ropes, a rope turning, along with the twisted ones, and two small ropes of one span of length, to turn the twisted one; then tie the ligament between the tendons towards the head of the twisted one, and the other ligament towards the feet of the other twisted one, and each assistant turns his twisted one to the whole limb, and the masters put the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with abundant honey, and then press it, and then place the edge of a plate of three inches long, to protect the joint from the gout and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until they are healed; and if anything happens at the end of the health, then administer medicines that are softening and soothing, with the method we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never does it appear in the back spine of the back, and consider that this is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which we should not have any presumption: perhaps it would cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of shoulder dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that the joints of the shoulder and the joints of the back do not come out only as dislocations, but also in a different way; and the joint of the back is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside than that, and less dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is such that when one joins the bad leg with the good one, it is longer and wider than the good ones, and cannot bend its knee to the fire; and it is the legs that are swollen from abscesses, because the complaint of the hip comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has this before are that he stands well on his leg according to completion; however, if he doubles over with pain in the groin, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and retains his urine, and swells up with anger, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has this after are that he cannot spread his groin, nor double over, and that leg is more bent than the other, and the anger is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated to the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The signs of this type of dislocation are such that if the dislocation is recent, and it remains according to its position, there is no cure; and there is no need for presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is recent, and it is of four types of dislocation, you must return the joint, and stretch it forward and backward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps if it returns, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then you must apply one strong minister, and stretch the leg firmly at two fingers, or at one finger that is tied above the knee; and other ministers extend their hand over the tail in a similar manner as they bite their hands off their shoulders, then pinch the side of the thigh with a soft finger; and some grip the head of the thigh; and stretch up and down all at once, until the pain is raised from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to treat its similarity. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to feel the pain on the healthy side of the shoulder, then place the elbow under the root of the armpit, and the arm that is outside the arm pit, then extend the elbow above the arm pit, and towards the neck; then take other ministers to grasp the large arm of the misaligned shoulder, and extend it to its proper form: it will return to its arm now; and this method of dislocation is less heavy than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not press it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary to tie the two evil legs together with a very strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the evil leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then hang it suspended by the head of a stick, and let the other arm be hanging down two arms' length from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the neck of the chicken, and another minister to hold the evil leg, who should grasp it firmly, for the joint is now returning.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is on the other side, then cut the evil leg as we have said in the one with gout, and pull the ligament properly above the evil leg, and also above the foot; then put two ties, one at the head and the other at the feet, then fold the tie between the thighs of the evil leg in the correct form; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not bleed, then stretch each minister towards him, and let the patient hold the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the table, and press it as we have said in the gilbosite, and grind the bad parts against the clean side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the bad leg quickly, as I have said; and place the pain of being above the bad angle, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the bad leg downwards, or lift it up, but it should be as it was when the hip was dislocated backwards, as we have said of the position on the two hips; and it should be on its face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table; and it will be good when the bad legs extend their legs, and they will be even; then bend the knees, and put the plaster, and the bandage of a cloth, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are even, remove the bandage, and let it walk well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: namely, from within and without, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are such that you command the patient to bend his leg at the hip, and if he cannot bend it at the hip, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is done by making the patient sit with his back against your face, and placing his foot on yours; then take his shoulder in your hands and bring them between your elbows, then bend the two sides of the shoulder firmly; and another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the sign is that he can bend his leg at the hip lightly; and apply the plaster to it, and rub the leg against the hip, and loosen it strongly for three or four hours, then remove it; and do not work on the patient's other side until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are never splinted and never fully dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is bent, and it hurts when touched at the part where it is dislocated: the remedy is to gently extend it with your hands when it is splinted only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from the beginning, you must first straighten the misaligned bone, and hold it with your hands above the ankle; then take the rope to yourself at your right hand, and then at your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and tap the rope loudly in the upper part; and do this twice as we have said, pulling and taking the rope; if it returns, it is good; if not, if you start over again, it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, then make the misaligned bone lie on its back on the ground, and firmly fix the rope between its thighs, so that it does not bend the misaligned bone; then hold the ministers' thigh, and other ministers extend the rope to their hands or to the ligament, so that they can tie it above the knee of the misaligned bone; then extend each minister equally, and the ropes should be between the thighs of the misaligned bone to hold it while you are extending it; then put the misaligned bone equal to the dislocation in your hands, and other ministers hold the leg clean on the outside, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it does not go well, apply the plaster and poke through, and let the swelling form, and bind the foot to the leg, and keep the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the joint is not too stretched; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling does not go down, then take it off again on the third day or fourth, and let it walk for four days; and if it goes before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you pacify it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	for two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they should be gently extended towards labor, and this is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no part of the joint, then it is necessary that you make the patient sit with the injured limb straight out or on a flat table, and place your hand over what opens from these joints, then press firmly on your hand until it returns; and when it is equal, and there is nothing open, then remove the sole of the foot from the table for two fingers' width, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three hours, then release; and let him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and of dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often times the pain is deadly: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and do not know the art well, and have not used it long, and are not merciful and slow, and not hard; at the beginning of things, gently treat abscesses, and leave the pain in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, now reset the member to its place, as soon as the abscesses have come; and when the member is in place, then administer remedies for abscesses, and cure the wound, as it should be, with dry dressings; and if with dislocation there is a break, and small bones are crushed, take out the bone, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering into the path of fear, according to what I have said, for this is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and your body.
Amen	Amen
